Agent Cannot Discharge Buyer from the Price
Ruling on agent's power to discharge buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on an agent for purchase discharging the buyer from the price and explain the analogy (qiyas jaliy) used to derive it.

Core Idea
An agent cannot forgive the price because he does not own it — similar to not being able to gift the purchased item.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the limits of an agent's authority in a purchase contract. While the agent is empowered to buy on behalf of the principal, he does not own the price money. Therefore, he cannot absolve the buyer from paying, whether for free or via set-off. The ruling is derived through a clear analogy (qiyas jaliy) with gifting the purchased item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What action is the agent taking? Absolving the buyer from the price (ibra). What is the ruling? It is not permissible.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The original case (asl) is the agent gifting the purchased item after taking possession. That is not permissible because the agent does not own the item.
3
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the agent's lack of ownership over the item in the asl. Similarly, the agent lacks ownership over the price in the new case (far').
The illa is jaliy (obvious).
4
Apply the analogy to the new case
Just as gifting the item is not allowed, forgiving the price is not allowed. This includes both unconditional ibra and ibra bil-iwad (set-off).
Muqasah (set-off) is also ibra of the price.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i might hold that the agent can discharge because the contract is concluded. The Hanafi response is that the agent is only authorized for purchase, not forgiveness.
The practical difference: validity of the discharge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
اشرف البدایہ جلد قمر
تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا مشتری کو بری کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے وکیل کا قبضہ پر قبضہ کر کے پھر مشتری کو ہبہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال جب وکیل کیلئے ابراء بلا عوض جائز نہیں ہے تو ابراء بالعوض یعنی مقاصہ بھی اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے جائز نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Agency. Ashraf al-Bidayah, volume qamar. It is not permissible to [act]. Therefore, the agent's absolving the buyer is also not permissible. Just as it is not permissible for the agent, after taking possession of the purchased item, to gift it to the buyer. In any case, when discharging without compensation is not permissible for the agent, then discharging with compensation, i.e., set-off (muqasah), is also not permissible, by analogy (qiyas) on this.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah, states a ruling regarding the powers of an agent appointed to purchase (wakil bil-shira). The agent is authorized to buy on behalf of the principal, but he does not own the price money; the principal does. Therefore, the agent cannot discharge (ibra) the buyer from the obligation to pay the price, whether without compensation or even by way of set-off (muqasah) in exchange for something else. The proof is by qiyas: just as the agent cannot give away the purchased item (by gift) after taking possession, because he is not the owner, similarly he cannot forgive the price. This is an obvious analogy (qiyas jaliy) based on lack of ownership over the price. The ruling applies to the agent for purchase; for an agent for sale, different rules apply regarding the price.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibra'): Discharge from a debt; forgiving the obligation to pay the price.
مقاصہ (muqasah): Set-off; mutual cancellation of debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't an agent for purchase discharge the buyer from the price?
A) Because the agent does not own the price; it belongs to the principal
B) Because the contract is invalid
C) Because the buyer has already paid
D) Because the agent has no authority over the purchased item

Key Takeaway
An agent for purchase cannot discharge the buyer from the price, whether without compensation or by set-off, due to lack of ownership over the price.

Validity of Wakalah with Vague Description of the Object
Ruling and proof on invalidity of agency due to excessive ignorance about the object

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency with vague object descriptions and apply the condition that excessive ignorance (jahl fahish) invalidates the contract.

Core Idea
If the agent cannot determine what to buy due to vague description, the agency is void — jahl fahish invalidates.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, we examine a key rule of agency: the object of purchase must be described with sufficient specificity. The text provides both the ruling and the proof from al-Jami' al-Saghir, showing how excessive generality renders the contract invalid. Understanding this distinction helps you correctly structure agency appointments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The appointment of an agent to purchase something. The ruling is that the agency is invalid (batil) if the description is too vague, and valid (sahih) if type or estimated price is mentioned.
The ruling is about the validity of the agency contract itself, not the subsequent purchase.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The condition is that the agent must be able to execute the command with reasonable certainty. This requires the object (mawkil bihi) to be described specifically enough to avoid jahl fahish.
The condition is shart in the sense of a validity condition.
3
Identify the invalidating factor
Excessive ignorance (jahl fahish) about the object prevents the agent from knowing what to buy, making execution impossible. This occurs when the word used covers multiple types or genera.
The text gives examples: 'thawb' (garment), 'dabbah' (animal), 'dar' (house).
4
Examine the proof from al-Jami' al-Saghir
The proof text explicitly states that if someone says 'Buy me a garment, an animal, or a house,' the agency is void due to jahl fahish. The commentary explains why each term is problematic.
This is a naqli dalil from the core Hanafi text, carrying the weight of zahir al-riwayah.
5
Understand the cure
To make the agency valid, the principal must either mention the specific type (e.g., Turkish slave) or mention an estimated price (thaman taqdiriy). Even without specifying quality, the agency is valid because the remaining ignorance is minor (jahl yasir).
The principle: type removes jahl fahish; estimated price reduces ignorance sufficiently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
جب وکیل مؤکل کی مراد پر مطلع نہیں ہو سکا تو وکیل تعمیل حکم پر بھی قادر نہ ہوگا اور جس صورت میں وکیل تعمیل حکم پر قادر نہ ہو چونکہ اس صورت میں وکالت درست نہیں ہوتی اسلئے مذکورہ صورت میں توکیل درست نہ ہوگی۔
اور اگر مؤکل نے ایسا لفظ ذکر کیا جو بہت کی انواع کو شامل ہوتا ہے مثلاً غلام خریدنے کا وکیل کیا یا باندی خریدنے کا وکیل کیا تو یہ وکالت بھی درست نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن اگر اس کا تخمینی شمن بیان کیا یا اس کی نوع بیان کر دی تو یہ توکیل درست ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ شمن بیان کر دینے سے نوع معلوم ہو جاتی ہے اور نوع ذکر کرنے سے جہالت کم ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس جب نوع ذکر کرنے سے جہالت کم ہو گئی تو وکیل تحمیل حکم پر قادر ہوگا۔ اور جب وکیل تعمیل حکم پر قادر ہے تو اس صورت میں وکالت بھی درست ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کی مثال بیان . کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو غلام خریدنے کیلئے یا با نذی خریدنے کیلئے وکیل کیا تو یہ وکالت درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ غلام اور لفظ باندی بہت کی انواع کو شامل ہے۔ اسلئے کہ غلام اور باندی ترکی بھی ہوتے ہیں ۔ حبشی بھی ، ہندی بھی ، سندی بھی، اور مولد بھی اور مولد وہ ہے جو مملکت اسلامیہ میں پیدا ہوا ہو ۔ بعض نے کہا کہ مولد وہ عجمی شخص ہے جس نے عرب میں پرورش پائی ہو اور بعض نے کہا کہ مولد وہ ہے جس کا باپ ہندی اور ماں عربی ہو۔
بہر حال لفظ غلام اور لفظ باندی جب بہت سی انواع کو شامل ہے تو جہالت فاحشہ کی وجہ سے وکیل تعمیل حکم پر قادر نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب وکیل کیلئے مؤکل کے حکم کی تعمیل ناممکن ہوتی ہے۔ تو وکالت درست نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی وکالت درست نہ ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر اس کی نوع بیان کر دی۔ مثلا یہ کہا کہ ترکی غلام خرید کر لایا حبشی و غیرہ وغیرہ تو یہ توکیل جائز ہے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر نوع تو بیان نہیں کی لیکن اس کا تخمینی شمن بیان کر دیا تو بھی مذکورہ دلیل کی وجہ سے توکیل درست ہو جائے گی اور اگر مؤکل نے نوع بیان کر دی یا تخمینی شمن بیان کر دیا لیکن اس کا جید ہونا یار دی ہونا یا درمیانی ہونا بیان نہیں کیا تو بھی تو کیل جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جہالت کی یہ مقدار اتنی کم ہے جس کو وکالت برداشت کر لیتی ہے اور اتنی مقدار جہالت کی وکالت کے باب میں کوئی پرواہ نہیں کی جاتی۔ لہذا اس جہالت کے با وجو دوکالت درست ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ متن میں صفت سے امام قدوری کی مراد نوع ہے۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وکالت بالشراء کیلئے شی ء کی جنس اور نوع کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے اور یہ بات بیان کرنے کی ضرورت اسلئے پیش آئی۔ تا کہ صاحب قدوری کا کلام صاحب ہدایہ کے. کردہ قاعدہ شرعیہ کے موافق ہو جائے اور تمام مشائخ کی تصریحات کے موافق ہو جائے کیونکہ مشائخ نے جنس اور نوع کا بیان کرنا ہی
ضروری قرار دیا ہے۔
وکیل بالشراء کو کہا کہ میرے لئے کپڑایا چوپایہ یا مکان خرید و تو وکالت جہالت فاحشہ کی وجہ سے باطل ہے
وفى الجامع الصغير من قال لآخر اشتر لى ثوبا او دابة او دارا فالوكالة باطلة للجهالة الفاحشة فان الدابة في حقيقة اللغة اسم لما يدب على وجه الأرض وفى العرف يطلق على الخيل والحمار والبغل فقد جمع اجناسا وكذا الثوب لانه يتناول الملبوس من الاطلس الى الكساء ولهذا لا يصح تسميته مهرا وكذا الدار تشمل ما هو في معنى الاجناس لانها تختلف اختلافا فاحشا باختلاف الاغراض والجيران والمرافق والمحال والبلدان فيتعذر الامتثال

ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے سے کہا کہ تو میرے لئے کپڑایا چوپایہ یا مکان خرید کر تو جہالت فاحشہ کی وجہ سے وکالت باطل ہے کیونکہ دا بہ حقیقت لغویہ کے اعتبار سے اس چیز کا نام ہے جو زمین پر چلتا ہے اور عرف میں گھوڑے، گدھے اور فیچر پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ پس یہ لفظ کئی جنسوں کو جامع ہے اسی طرح کپڑا اسلئے کہ وہ اعلیٰ کپڑے سے لے کر ادنی کپڑے تک ہر ایسی چیز کو شامل ہے جو پہنی جائے اس وجہ سے کپڑے کو مہر بنانا درست نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح داران چیزوں کو شامل ہے جو اجناس کے معنی میں ہیں۔ اسلئے کہ دار، مقاصد، پڑوسیوں ،منافع محلوں اور شہروں کے اعتبار سے بہت مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا تعمیل متعد ر ہوگی۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ موکل اگر ایسا لفظ ذکر کرے جو بہت سی جنسوں کو شامل ہو تو جامع صغیر میں اس کی صورت اس طرح مذکور ہے اگر کسی نے دوسرے آدمی سے کہا کہ تو میرے لئے کپڑا خرید کر لایا چوپایہ خرید کر لایا مکان خرید کر دے تو یہ وکالت باطل ہے۔
چہ مؤکل تخمینی شمن بھی بیان کر دے۔ اسکے باوجود اگر وکیل نے خرید کیا تویہ خرید نا خود وکیل کیلئے ہو گا۔ مؤکل کیلئے نہ ہو گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ را بہ ثوب، اور دار میں جہالت فاحشہ ہے اس طور پر کہ دابہ کے لغت کے اعتبار سے حقیقی معنی اس چیز کے ہیں جو زمین پر چلتی ہو اور عرف میں دابہ کا اطلاق گھوڑے، گدھے اور خچر پر ہوتا ہے۔ بہر صورت دابہ کے حقیقی معنی مراد ہوں یا عرفی معنی دونوں صورتوں میں لفظ را بہ مختلف جنسوں کو شامل ہے۔ اور کسی لفظ کا مختلف قسم کی جنسوں کو شامل ہونا اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ اس لفظ میں فاحش اور کثیر جہالت ہے۔ اسی طرح لفظ ثوب ( کپڑا) چونکہ اطلس ( ریشمی کپڑے ( یعنی اعلیٰ قسم کے کپڑے سے لے کر ادنی قسم کے کپڑے تک ہر طرح کے پہنے جانے والے کپڑے کو شامل ہے۔ اسلئے ثواب کے لفظ میں بھی کثیر اور فاحش جہالت ہوگی ہی جہالت فاحشہ کی وجہ سے ( ثوب) کپڑے کو مہر قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے۔ یعنی کپڑے کے لفظ سے اگر مہر بیان کیا تو یہ معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ مہرشل لازم ہوگا۔ بہر حال کپڑے کا لفظ بھی چونکہ مختلف اجناس کو شامل ہے۔ اسلئے کپڑے کے لفظ میں بھی جہالت فاحشہ ہے۔ اسی طرح لفظ دار ( مکان ) اگر چہ حقیقتاً مختلف اجناس کو شامل نہیں ہوتا لیکن ایسے مکانوں کو شامل ہوتا ہے جو مختلف اجناس کے معنی میں ہیں کیونکہ مکانوں میں مالیت کے اعتبار سے بہت زیادہ تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ مکانوں کی اغراض مختلف ہوتی ہیں۔ مثلا ایک مکان کاروباری دفتر کیلئے موزوں ہے مگر رہائش کیلئے مناسب نہیں ہے اور اس کا برعکس اور پڑوسیوں کے اعتبار سے بھی مکان مالیت میں ہے متفاوت ہوتے ہیں۔ مثلاً ایک مکان ایسا ہے جس کے پڑوس میں شریف لوگ، بھلے لوگ آباد ہیں اور ایک مکان ایسا ہے جس کے پڑوس میں انتہائی ناہنجار اور گھٹیا قسم کے لوگ آباد ہیں۔ ان دونوں مکانوں کی قیمتیں متفاوت ہوں گی۔ منافع کے اعتبار سے بھی مکان مالیت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں۔ مثلاً ایک مکان ایسا ہے جس میں دھوپ بھی آتی ہے اور ہوا بھی مسجد سے بھی قریب ہے اور شاہراہ سے بھی ۔ اور ایک مکان ایسا ہے جس میں یہ سہولتیں میسر نہیں ہیں۔ تو ان دونوں مکانوں کی بھی قیمتیں متفاوت ہوں گی۔ محلوں کے اعتبار سے بھی مالیت میں تفاوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً ایک مکان ایسے محلہ میں واقع ہے جہاں گندگی اور تعفن رہتا ہے اور ایک مکان ایسے محلہ میں واقع ہے جہاں صفائی ستھرائی کا معقول نظم ہے اور شہری سہولتیں بھی فراہم ہیں۔ تو ان دونوں مکانات میں بھی مالیت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت ہو گا۔ اور شہروں کے اعتبار سے بھی مکانات کی مالیت میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ جو مکان دیلی جیسے شہر میں ہے اسکی مالیت اسی درجہ کے اس مکان سے بہت زیادہ ہوگی ۔ جو دیوبند جیسے شہر میں ہے۔ بہر حال جب ان وجوہ سے مکانات مالیت کے اعتبار سے متفاوت ہیں تو لفظ دار چونکہ ہر طرح کے مکان کو شامل ہے اسلئے لفظ دار اگر چہ حقیقتاً مختلف اجناس کے مکانوں کو شامل نہیں ہے لیکن یہ مکانات مالیت کے تفاوت کی وجہ
Book of Agency: When the agent cannot know the principal's intent, the agent will not be able to execute the command. And in the case where the agent is unable to execute the command, since agency is not valid in that case, therefore in the mentioned case the appointment of agency will not be valid. And if the principal mentions a word that includes many types, for example he appoints an agent to buy a male slave or to buy a female slave, then this agency also is not valid. But if he mentions its estimated price or mentions its type, then this agency becomes valid. Because by mentioning the price the type becomes known, and by mentioning the type ignorance is reduced. So when ignorance is reduced by mentioning the type, the agent will be able to execute the command. And when the agent is able to execute the command, then in that case agency will be valid. The author of Hidayah, while giving an example, said: If a person appoints another as agent to buy a male slave or to buy a female slave, then this agency is not correct. Because the word 'male slave' and 'female slave' include many types. That is because male and female slaves may be Turkish, Abyssinian, Indian, Sindhi, and muwallad. Muwallad is one who was born in the Islamic lands. Some said muwallad is a non-Arab person who grew up among Arabs, and some said muwallad is one whose father is Indian and mother is Arab. In any case, when the word 'male slave' and 'female slave' include many types, then due to excessive ignorance the agent will not be able to execute the command. And when execution of the principal's command is impossible for the agent, then agency is not valid. Therefore in the mentioned case also agency will not be valid. Yes, if he mentions its type, for example he said: Bring a Turkish slave, not Abyssinian etc., then this appointment is permissible. Similarly, if he did not mention the type but mentioned its estimated price, then also due to the mentioned reason the agency becomes valid. And if the principal mentioned the type or mentioned the estimated price but did not mention whether it is high quality, low quality, or medium, then also the agency is permissible. Because this amount of ignorance is so small that agency tolerates it, and such a small amount of ignorance is not considered in the chapter of agency. Therefore, despite this ignorance, the agency will be valid. The author of Hidayah said: In the matn, 'sifah' (description) means type according to Imam Quduri. Now the meaning is that for agency in purchase, it is necessary to mention the genus and type of the thing. And the need to mention this arose so that the statement of Imam Quduri becomes in accordance with the legal principle set by the author of Hidayah and in accordance with the explicit statements of all the mashayikh, because the mashayikh have declared the mention of genus and type as necessary. [The text continues with the quote from al-Jami' al-Saghir and its explanation.]
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the validity of an agency contract (wakalah) when the object to be purchased is described vaguely. The ruling is a ruling_statement with proof. The central principle is that a wakalah is valid only if the agent can execute the principal's command with reasonable certainty. If the description of the object is so vague that it encompasses multiple distinct types, the agent cannot know what exactly to buy, and thus the agency is void due to excessive ignorance (jahl fahish). The text first explains that if the principal uses a word that covers many types (e.g., 'slave' without specifying Turkish, Abyssinian, etc.), the agency is invalid. However, if the principal specifies the type (e.g., Turkish slave) or mentions an estimated price, the ignorance is reduced sufficiently, and the agency becomes valid. Even if the quality (high, low, medium) is not specified, the agency remains valid because such minor ignorance is tolerated. The author then quotes al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani as a proof text. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is stated that if someone says to another, 'Buy for me a garment, or an animal, or a house,' the agency is void due to excessive ignorance. The reason is that the word 'dabbah' (animal) in its literal sense means anything that walks on the earth, but in custom (urf) it refers to horses, donkeys, and mules, thus covering multiple genera. Similarly, 'thawb' (garment) includes everything from high-quality silk (atlas) to coarse cloth, so it is so general that it cannot even be used as a valid dower (mahr). The word 'dar' (house) also covers houses that differ vastly in value due to differences in purpose, neighbors, facilities, location, and city. Therefore, compliance is impossible. The commentary emphasizes that this ruling is based on the principle that the agent must be able to fulfill the command, and excessive ignorance prevents that. The Hanafi position is clear: the object of an agency must be described with sufficient specificity to avoid jahl fahish. This is a zahir al-riwayah position as it appears in al-Jami' al-Saghir, one of the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
جہالت فاحشہ (jahālah fāḥishah): Excessive ignorance or vagueness that prevents the agent from knowing what is intended, thereby invalidating the contract.
دابہ (dābbah): Literally any creature that crawls on the earth; in common usage (urf) it refers specifically to horses, donkeys, and mules.
ثوب (thawb): Garment or cloth covering anything from high-quality silk to coarse fabric.
دار (dār): House or dwelling, but houses vary greatly in value due to location, facilities, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the proof from al-Jami' al-Saghir, which of the following words used in an agency to purchase renders the contract void due to jahl fahish?
A) A specific laptop model (e.g., Dell XPS 13)
B) A garment (thawb)
C) A Turkish slave
D) A house in a specified neighborhood

Key Takeaway
Agency for purchase is valid only if the object is described with sufficient specificity to avoid excessive ignorance; mentioning the type or an estimated price suffices.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Agency in Sarf and Salam Contracts
Ruling on validity of agency for Sarf and Salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency in Sarf and Salam contracts and explain the distinction between executing and accepting Salam.

Core Idea
Agency is valid for executing Sarf and Salam, but invalid for accepting Salam because the agent's liability conflicts with the benefit.

You already know that agency (wakalah) is generally permissible for any act the principal can perform. But Islamic law recognizes exceptions where delegation leads to injustice. This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a critical distinction: why a buyer in a Salam contract can appoint an agent, but the seller cannot. Understanding this exception sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists protect fairness in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
State the two rulings: agency in executing Sarf and Salam is permissible (mubah); agency in accepting Salam is prohibited (la yajuz). Recognise that the passage treats Sarf and Salam similarly for execution, but distinguishes acceptance of Salam.
2
Trace the general principle
Recall the base rule from the beginning of the wakalah chapter: a person can appoint an agent for any contract he can perform himself (daf'an li'l-hajah). This principle supports agency for executing Sarf and Salam.
Quduri says: 'A person can appoint an agent for what he can do himself.'
3
Locate the exception and its proof
Identify the exception: the seller (muslam ilayh) cannot appoint an agent to accept a Salam contract. The proof (talil): the agent would be selling grain on his own liability (dhimma) while the price goes to the principal. This is like selling one's own property on condition that the price is for a third party, which is invalid.
The agent assumes debt without benefit, creating an injustice.
4
Address the potential objection
Anticipate the objection: if the seller can accept Salam himself, why can't he delegate? The response: the general rule is overridden here because the agent's assuming liability without benefit creates a prohibited arrangement (fasid). The exception blocks a means to harm (sadd al-dhara'i).
The rule is 'al-'umur bi-maqasidiha' – the agent's intention would be to serve the principal, but the contract's effect is unjust.
5
Summarise the practical consequence
In practice: the buyer can validly use an agent to execute a Salam contract; the seller must accept the contract personally. If a seller appoints an agent, the contract is invalid and the agent's action is not binding on the principal.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi school; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عقد صرف اور سلم میں وکالت جائز ہے
قال ويجوز التوكيل بعقد الصرف والسلم لانه عقد يملكه بنفسه فيملك التوكيل به دفعا للحاجة على مامر ومراده التوكيل بالاسلام دون قبول السلم لان ذالك لا يجوز فان الوكيل يبيع طعاما في ذمته على ان يكون الثمن لغيره ولهذا لا يجوز
ترجمہ اور عقد صرف اور سلم کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسلئے کہ یہ ایسا عقد ہے جس کو موکل خود کر سکتا ہے۔ پس حاجت دور کرنے کیلئے اس کے واسطے وکیل کرنے کا بھی اختیار ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ گذر چکا اور مصنف کی مراد عقد سلم کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا ہے نہ کہ عقد سلم قبول کرنے کیلئے کیونکہ یہ تو کیل جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ وکیل ایسا غلہ بیچے گا جو اس کے ذمہ میں ہو اس شرط پر کہ ثمن اسکے غیر کیلئے ہو اور یہ بات جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ عقد صرف اور عقد سلم کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے عقد صرف یا عقد سلم منعقد کرنے کا کسی کو وکیل کیا تو جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل عقد صرف اور عقد سلم بذات خود منعقد کرنے کا مالک ہے اور اول باب وکالت میں گذر چکا ہے کہ انسان جس عقد کو خود منعقد کر سکتا ہے ضرورت دور کرنے کیلئے اسکے واسطے دوسرے کو وکیل بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ پس جب موکل عقد صر ف اور مقد سلم بذات خود منعقد کر سکتا ہے تو اس کیلئے وکیل کرنے کا مالک بھی ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ایک تو عقد سلم کو منعقد کرنا ہے اور ایک عقد سلم کو قبول کرنا ہے۔ عقد سلم کو منعقد کرنا تو رب السلام کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے اور قبول کرنا مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے۔ پس متن میں مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ عقد سلم منعقد کرنے کیلئے رب اسلم وکیل کرسکتا ہے لیکن عقد سلم قبول کرنے کیلئے مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
عدم جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ کا وکیل ایسا اناج فروخت کرے گا جو اس کے ذمہ میں ادھار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مسلم فیہ مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ میں ادھار ہوتی ہے لیکن جب مسلم الیہ نے وکیل مقرر کر لیا اور وکیل ہی نے عقد سلم کو قبول کیا ہے تو مسلم فیہ وکیل کے ذمہ میں ادھار ہوگی ۔ اس شرط پر کہ ثمن دوسرے کیلئے یعنی مؤکل کیلئے ہو۔ حالانکہ یہ نا جائز ہے کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنی مملوکہ چیز کو اس شرط پر فروخت کرے کہ شمن دوسرے کیلے ہوتو ہینا جائز ہے۔ پس اس طرح اگر دین یعنی مسلم فیہ وکیل اپنے ذمہ میں واجب کرے اور من مؤکل کیلئے ہوتو یہ بھی ناجائز ہوگا۔ اعتراض لیکن اس پر یہ اعتراض ہو سکتا ہے کہ اول باب میں بیان کردہ قاعدہ کے مطابق مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے عقد سلم قبول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا بھی نا جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ کیونکہ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ انسان جس کام کو خود کرسکتا ہے اس کے واسطے وکیل بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ پس جب مسلم الیہ عقد سلم خود قبول کر سکتا ہے تو اس کو قبول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا بھی جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔
Agency in the contract of Sarf and Salam is permissible.
He said: It is permissible to appoint an agent for the contract of Sarf and Salam because it is a contract that the principal can perform himself, so he has the right to appoint an agent for it to fulfill the need, as has passed. And his intent is agency for Salam (as seller/buyer) not acceptance of Salam, because that is not permissible. For the agent sells food on his own liability on the condition that the price is for someone else, so this is not permissible.
Translation: And appointing an agent for the contract of Sarf and Salam is permissible. Because it is a contract that the principal can do himself. So to fulfill the need, he will have the right to appoint an agent for it, as has passed. And the author's intent is agency for executing Salam, not for accepting Salam, because that is not permissible. Because the agent would sell grain on his own liability on the condition that the price is for someone else, and this is not permissible.
Explanation: Al-Quduri said: Appointing an agent for the contract of Sarf and Salam is permissible; that is, if a person appoints someone as agent to execute a Sarf or Salam contract, it is permissible. The proof is that the principal himself can execute Sarf and Salam, and it has passed in the beginning of the chapter of agency that a person can appoint an agent for what he can do himself to fulfill the need. So when the principal can execute Sarf and Salam himself, he also has the right to appoint an agent.
The author of Al-Hidayah says: There are two things: executing a Salam contract and accepting a Salam contract. Executing a Salam contract is done by the buyer (rabb al-salam), and accepting it is done by the seller (muslam ilayh). So the author's intent in the text is that the buyer can appoint an agent to execute Salam, but the seller cannot appoint an agent to accept Salam, and that is not permissible.
Proof of impermissibility: The agent of the seller would sell grain that is on his own liability, because the salam commodity is on the seller's liability. When the seller appoints an agent and the agent accepts the Salam, then the salam commodity becomes on the agent's liability, on the condition that the price is for someone else (the principal). This is impermissible because if a person sells his own property on the condition that the price is for someone else, it is not permissible. Similarly, if the agent incurs a debt (the salam commodity) on his own liability and the price is for the principal, it is also impermissible.
Objection: But there is an objection: According to the rule mentioned in the beginning of the chapter, agency for accepting Salam should also be permissible, because the rule is that a person can appoint an agent for what he can do himself. Since the seller can accept Salam himself, he should be able to appoint an agent to do so.
[The response is implied: the rule has an exception here due to the share of the commodity being on the agent's liability.]
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of agency in two specific types of contracts: Sarf (currency exchange) and Salam (forward sale). The commentator begins by stating the permissibility of appointing an agent for these contracts based on the general principle that any contract a principal can perform himself may be delegated to an agent to meet practical needs. However, a crucial distinction is made regarding Salam: agency is valid for executing the Salam contract (i.e., the buyer's side, where the price is paid in advance) but not for accepting Salam (i.e., the seller's side, who receives the price and must deliver goods later). The reason for the prohibition is that if a seller appoints an agent to accept a Salam contract, the agent would be selling goods on his own credit (since the seller is liable for delivery) while the price goes to the principal. This arrangement is invalid because it involves selling one's own debt (or goods to be delivered) for the benefit of another, akin to selling property on condition the price goes to a third party. The passage acknowledges a potential objection based on the general rule, but the specific rule overrides due to the element of injustice (the agent assuming personal liability without benefit). This ruling is found in Al-Hidayah and is consistent with the Hanafi position that agency in accepting Salam is not valid.

Key Terms
صرف (ṣarf): A contract for exchanging gold and silver (or currency) in Islamic law.
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the buyer pays the price in advance and the seller delivers the goods at a future date.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer in a Salam contract who pays the price in advance.
مسلم إليه (muslam ilayh): The seller in a Salam contract who receives the price and must deliver the goods later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Salam contract, which party can appoint an agent according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only the seller (muslam ilayh) can appoint an agent
B) The buyer (rabb al-salam) can appoint an agent to execute the contract, but the seller cannot appoint an agent to accept it
C) Both buyer and seller can appoint agents
D) Neither party can appoint an agent for Salam

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, agency is valid for executing Sarf and Salam contracts, but invalid for accepting Salam because the agent would assume personal liability for delivery without receiving the price, which is an impermissible arrangement.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Agency for Sarf and Salam Contracts
Stating the permissibility of agency in sarf and salam and clarifying the limitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency for sarf and salam contracts and explain why the seller cannot delegate the acceptance of salam.

Core Idea
Agency is allowed for contracts one can do oneself, but an exception granted by text cannot be extended to an agent.

This passage clarifies the permissibility of appointing an agent for sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance sale) contracts. It establishes a general rule—one can delegate what one can do—but then introduces a critical limitation: in salam, only the buyer (rabb al-salam) may appoint an agent to conclude the contract; the seller (muslam ilayh) cannot delegate acceptance. The reason lies in the exceptional nature of salam itself, which is permitted by hadith despite the non-existence of the object. Understanding this distinction deepens your grasp of the Hanafi principle that text-based exceptions are confined to their specific context and cannot be extended by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Read the opening sentence: it permits agency for sarf and salam because the principal can perform the contract himself. Note the underlying principle: one can delegate any act one is capable of doing personally, to fulfill a need.
This principle was established in the first chapter of Wakalah.
2
Spot the distinction
The author then specifies that 'agency for concluding salam' (tawkeel bil islam) is intended, not 'agency for accepting salam' (qabul al-salam). This distinction is crucial: the buyer can appoint an agent, but the seller cannot.
Concluding salam is from the buyer; accepting salam is from the seller.
3
Understand the reason for impermissibility
If the seller appoints an agent to accept salam, the agent would become liable for the commodity (muslam fih) on his own debt while the price goes to the principal. This is analogous to selling one's own goods for another's benefit, which is invalid.
The agent sells grain on his own liability for a price that belongs to the principal.
4
Analyze the objection and response
A hypothetical objector argues: if the seller can accept salam himself, why can't he delegate it? The Hanafi response uses the principle that salam itself is an exception to qiyas (analogy). It was allowed by the Prophet's hadith despite the missing object. Such exceptions are text-specific and cannot be extended by analogy to the agent.
The hadith: 'He forbade selling what one does not possess and granted a concession for salam.'
5
Extract the legal principle
Conclude: 'What is established by text contrary to qiyas is confined to the text.' This principle prevents the extension of exceptional rulings to new cases, such as agency.
This is a key Hanafi usul maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز التوكيل بعقد الصرف والسلم لانه عقد يملكه بنفسه فيملك التوكيل به دفعا للحاجة على مامر ومراده التوكيل بالاسلام دون قبول السلم لان ذالك لا يجوز فان الوكيل يبيع طعاما في ذمته على ان يكون الثمن لغيره ولهذا لا يجوز
ترجمہ اور عقد صرف اور سلم کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسلئے کہ یہ ایسا عقد ہے جس کو موکل خود کر سکتا ہے۔ پس حاجت دور کرنے کیلئے اس کے واسطے وکیل کرنے کا بھی اختیار ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ گذر چکا اور مصنف کی مراد عقد سلم کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا ہے نہ کہ عقد سلم قبول کرنے کیلئے کیونکہ یہ تو کیل جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ وکیل ایسا غلہ بیچے گا جو اس کے ذمہ میں ہو اس شرط پر کہ ثمن اسکے غیر کیلئے ہو اور یہ بات جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ عقد صرف اور عقد سلم کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے عقد صرف یا عقد سلم منعقد کرنے کا کسی کو وکیل کیا تو جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل عقد صرف اور عقد سلم بذات خود منعقد کرنے کا مالک ہے اور اول باب وکالت میں گذر چکا ہے کہ انسان جس عقد کو خود منعقد کر سکتا ہے ضرورت دور کرنے کیلئے اسکے واسطے دوسرے کو وکیل بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ پس جب موکل عقد صرف اور عقد سلم بذات خود منعقد کر سکتا ہے تو اس کیلئے وکیل کرنے کا مالک بھی ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ایک تو عقد سلم کو منعقد کرنا ہے اور ایک عقد سلم کو قبول کرنا ہے۔ عقد سلم کو منعقد کرنا تو رب السلام کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے اور قبول کرنا مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے۔ پس متن میں مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ عقد سلم منعقد کرنے کیلئے رب السلم وکیل کرسکتا ہے لیکن عقد سلم قبول کرنے کیلئے مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
عدم جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ کا وکیل ایسا اناج فروخت کرے گا جو اس کے ذمہ میں ادھار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مسلم فیہ مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ میں ادھار ہوتی ہے لیکن جب مسلم الیہ نے وکیل مقرر کر لیا اور وکیل ہی نے عقد سلم کو قبول کیا ہے تو مسلم فیہ وکیل کے ذمہ میں ادھار ہوگی ۔ اس شرط پر کہ ثمن دوسرے کیلئے یعنی مؤکل کیلئے ہو۔ حالانکہ یہ نا جائز ہے کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنی مملوکہ چیز کو اس شرط پر فروخت کرے کہ ثمن دوسرے کیلئے ہو تو ہی نا جائز ہے۔ پس اس طرح اگر دین یعنی مسلم فیہ وکیل اپنے ذمہ میں واجب کرے اور ثمن مؤکل کیلئے ہو تو یہ بھی ناجائز ہوگا۔ اعتراض لیکن اس پر یہ اعتراض ہو سکتا ہے کہ اول باب میں بیان کردہ قاعدہ کے مطابق مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے عقد سلم قبول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا بھی نا جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ کیونکہ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ انسان جس کام کو خود کرسکتا ہے اس کے واسطے وکیل بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ پس جب مسلم الیہ عقد سلم خود قبول کر سکتا ہے تو اس کو قبول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا بھی جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ بھی عقد سلم قبول کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہو کیونکہ عقد سلم میں مسلم فیہ ( مبیع ) معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد سلم نا جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ لیکن رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نـهـي عـن بـيـع ما ليس عند الانسان ورخص فی السلم کی وجہ سے مفلسوں کی حاجت دور کرنے کیلئے۔ خلاف قیاس عقد سلم مشروع کیا گیا ہے اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ مور دنص پر منحصر رہتی ہے۔ اس پر دوسرے کو قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا عقد سلم کو خلاف قیاس مسلم الیہ تو قبول کرنے کا مجاز ہے لیکن اس کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
He said: It is permissible to appoint an agent for the contract of currency exchange (sarf) and salam (advance sale), because it is a contract which the principal can perform himself, so he can appoint an agent for it to fulfill a need, as previously mentioned. And his (the author's) intention is agency for concluding salam, not for accepting salam, because that is not permissible. For the agent would sell grain on his own liability on condition that the price be for someone else, and this is not permissible.
Translation: And it is permissible to appoint an agent for the contracts of sarf and salam. Because this is a contract which the principal can perform himself. So to meet a need, he can authorize an agent for it, as has passed. And the author's intention is agency for concluding the salam contract, not for accepting the salam contract, because that is not permissible. For the agent would sell grain that is on his own liability on condition that the price be for someone else, and this is not permissible.
Commentary: Imam al-Quduri said that it is permissible to appoint an agent for sarf and salam, i.e., if a person appoints someone as agent to conclude a sarf or salam contract, it is permissible. The evidence is that the principal himself is capable of concluding sarf and salam contracts, and in the first chapter of Wakalah it has passed that a person can appoint another as agent for what he himself can do, to meet a need. So when the principal can himself conclude sarf and salam, he has the right to appoint an agent for it.
The author of al-Hidayah says: There are two things: concluding the salam contract and accepting the salam contract. Concluding the salam is done by the buyer (rabb al-salam), and accepting is done by the seller (muslam ilayh). So in the text, the author means that the buyer can appoint an agent to conclude the salam, but the seller cannot appoint an agent to accept the salam.
The evidence for impermissibility is that the agent of the seller would sell grain that is on his own liability, because the subject matter (muslam fih) is on the liability of the seller. But when the seller appoints an agent and the agent accepts the salam, the muslam fih becomes on the liability of the agent, on condition that the price be for someone else, i.e., the principal. This is impermissible because if a person sells his owned property on condition that the price be for someone else, it is impermissible. So similarly, if the debt (muslam fih) becomes obligatory on the agent and the price is for the principal, it is also impermissible.
Objection: But it can be objected that according to the rule mentioned in the first chapter, it should also be permissible for the seller to appoint an agent to accept salam, because the rule is that a person can appoint an agent for what he himself can do. Since the seller can himself accept salam, he should be able to appoint an agent for it.
Answer: The answer is that analogical reasoning (qiyas) would require that even the seller himself should not be permitted to accept salam, because in the salam contract, the subject matter is non-existent, so the contract should be impermissible. But due to the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibiting selling what one does not possess and granting concession for salam, the salam contract is legislated contrary to qiyas to meet the need of the needy. And what is established by a text contrary to qiyas is confined to the text; applying qiyas to it is not correct. Therefore, the seller is permitted to accept salam contrary to qiyas, but it is not permissible for him to appoint an agent for it.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage expands upon the ruling of agency (wakalah) in the specific contracts of sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance sale). It begins by stating the general rule: both are permissible for agency because the principal can perform them himself, so he can delegate them to fulfill a need. The author then makes a crucial distinction: agency for the concluding of the salam contract (from the buyer's side) is permissible, but agency for the acceptance of salam (from the seller's side) is not. The reason is that if the seller appoints an agent to accept salam, the agent would incur a debt (the muslam fih) on his own liability while the price goes to the principal. This resembles selling one's own property with the condition that the price goes to another, which is invalid. A potential objection is raised: since the seller can accept salam himself, why can he not delegate it according to the general principle that one can delegate what one can do? The answer resolves this by pointing out that the very permissibility of salam itself is an exception to analogy (qiyas) – it is allowed by the Prophet's hadith despite the non-existence of the sold item. Such an exception is text-specific and cannot be extended by analogy to cover agency. Thus, the seller's exception is limited to his own action; his agent cannot benefit from it. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that 'what is established by text contrary to qiyas is confined to the text'.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakālah): Agency; the delegation of authority to another to perform a legal act on one's behalf.
صرف (ṣarf): Currency exchange; a contract for the sale of gold, silver, or money of the same or different types.
سلم (salam): Advance sale; a contract where the price is paid in advance for a defined commodity to be delivered later.
موکل (muwakkil): Principal; the person who appoints an agent.
وکیل (wakīl): Agent; the person appointed to act on behalf of the principal.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.
خلاف قیاس (khilāf al-qiyās): Contrary to analogy; a ruling established by textual evidence that does not follow analogical reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, who may appoint an agent to conclude the contract?
A) Both the buyer and the seller.
B) Only the buyer (rabb al-salam).
C) Only the seller (muslam ilayh).
D) Neither, because salam cannot be delegated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, agency is permissible for sarf and salam, but only the buyer in salam can delegate; the seller's exceptional permission is personal and cannot be extended to an agent.

Effect of Agent's Separation Before Possession in Sarf and Salam
Explaining that the contract becomes void if the agent separates before possession, unlike a messenger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent separates before possession in sarf/salam and distinguish it from the case of a messenger.

Core Idea
In sarf and salam, the agent's separation before possession voids the contract; the principal's separation does not matter, and a messenger's possession is irrelevant.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical nuance in sarf and salam contracts involving an agent. The core ruling is straightforward: if the agent and the counterparty separate from the contract session without taking possession, the contract becomes void (batil). However, the commentary clarifies that this applies only to the agent's separation, not the principal's, because the agent is the contracting party ('aqid). Furthermore, it contrasts the agent with a messenger (rasul), whose possession is not considered as that of the contractor. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the possession-in-session condition in agency transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the act
Recognize that the ruling applies to sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance payment) contracts. The act under scrutiny is the separation (iftiraq) of the agent from the counterparty before taking possession (qabd).
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that such separation renders the contract batil (void). The condition for validity—possession during the contract session—is not fulfilled.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the agent's role
Understand that the agent (wakil) is the contractor ('aqid). Therefore, the right to take possession belongs to him, and his separation is legally significant. The principal's separation is irrelevant because he is not a party to the contract.
The agent may be a minor or restricted slave; his possession remains valid for this purpose.
4
Contrast with a messenger
A messenger (rasul) only conveys speech; the contract is between the sender and the other party. Therefore, the messenger's possession is not that of a contractor, so his separation does not affect the contract's validity.
The contract remains valid if the messenger separates, because the condition applies to the actual parties.
5
Apply to both sarf and salam
The condition of possession in the session applies to both: in sarf, both exchanged items must be possessed; in salam, the principal (ra's al-mal) must be possessed by the seller.
The agent's separation before any such possession voids the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان فارق الوكيل صاحبه قبل القبض بطل العقد لوجود الافتراق من غير قبض ولا يعتبر مفارقة المؤكل لانه ليس بعاقد والمستحق بالعقد قبض العاقد وهو الوكيل فيصح قبضه وان كان لا يتعلق به الحقوق كالصبي والعبد المحجور عليه بخلاف الرسولين لان الرسالة فى العقد لا فى القبض وينتقل كلامه الى المرسل فصار قبض الرسول قبض غير العاقد فلم يصح
ترجمہ: پس اگر وکیل قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اپنے ساتھی سے جدا ہو گیا تو عقد باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ بغیر قبضہ کے جدا ہونا پایا گیا اور مؤکل کا جدا ہونا معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ موکل عقد کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور عقد کی وجہ سے قبضہ کا مستحق عاقد ہوتا ہے اور وہ وکیل ہے پس وکیل ہی کا قبضہ صحیح ہوگا۔ اگر چہ اس کے ساتھ حقوق متعلق نہ ہوتے ہوں جیسے بچ اور غیر ماذون، غلام، برخلاف ایلچیوں کے اسلئے کہ ایلچی کرنا عقد کرنے کیلئے ہے نہ کہ قبضہ کرنے کیلئے اور ایلچی کا کلام بھیجنے والے کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس چونکہ ایلچی کا قبضہ کرنا غیر عاقد کا قبضہ کرنا ہوا۔ اسلئے یہ قبضہ صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عقد صرف یا عقد سلم کرنے والا وکیل اور اس کا وہ ساتھی جس نے اس کے ساتھ عقد صرف یا عقد سلم کیا ہے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے دونوں جدا ہو گئے تو یہ عقد باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عقد صرف کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس عقد میں دونوں عوضین پر قبضہ متفق ہو جائے اور عقد سلم درست ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس عقد میں رأس المال پر مسلم الیہ کا قبضہ تحقیق ہو جائے۔ پس جب وکیل اور دوسرا عاقد قبضہ کیلئے بغیر مجلس سے جدا ہو گئے تو عقد صرف اور عقد سلم کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط نہیں پائی گئی اور جب شرط صحت نہیں پائی گئی تو عقد صرف اور عقد سلم باطل ہو جائے گا۔
صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مجلس عقد سے مؤکل کے جدا ہونے کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ موکل عاقد نہیں ہوتا اور عقد کی وجہ سے قبضہ کا مستحق عاقد ہوتا ہے اور عاقد وکیل ہے۔ لہذا بدل صرف پر وکیل کا قبضہ صحیح ہوگا۔ نہ کہ مؤکل کا وکیل خواہ ان لوگوں میں سے ہو جن کے ساتھ حقوق عقد متعلق ہوتے ہیں۔ جیسے بالغ، عبد ماذون لہ فی التجارہ۔ خواہ ان لوگوں میں سے ہو جن کے ساتھ حقوق عقد متعلق نہیں ہوتے جیسے نابالغ اور عبد غیر ماذون لہ اور قبضہ کا مستحق عاقد اسلئے ہوتا ہے کہ عقد صرف میں قبضہ عقد کا اور عبد غیر ماذون لہ تمہ اور تکملہ ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا جس سے عقد صرف صادر ہو گا اس کی طرف سے قبضہ بھی صحیح ہوگا اور مذکورہ صورت میں چونکہ عقد صرف وکیل سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے قبضہ بھی وکیل کا صحیح ہوگا اور جب قبضہ وکیل کا صحیح ہے تو مجلس عقد سے اس کا جدا ہونا معتبر ہوگا۔ مؤکل کا جدا ہونا
If the agent separates from his counterparty before taking possession, the contract becomes void, due to the occurrence of separation without possession. And the separation of the principal is not considered, because he is not the contractor. The one entitled to possession by the contract is the contractor, and he is the agent, so his possession is valid, even if rights do not attach to him, such as a minor or a restricted slave. Unlike the two messengers, because the messengership is for the contract, not for possession, and his speech transfers to the sender. So the possession of the messenger becomes the possession of one who is not the contractor, so it is not valid.
Translation: So if the agent separates from his companion before taking possession, the contract becomes void, because separation without possession has occurred. And the separation of the principal is not considered, because the principal is not the contractor. The one entitled to possession due to the contract is the contractor, and he is the agent. So the agent's possession is valid, even if rights do not attach to him, like a child or a non-permitted slave. Unlike the messengers, because the messengership is for the contract, not for possession, and the messenger's speech is transferred to the sender. So since the messenger's possession is the possession of a non-contractor, this possession is not valid.
Commentary: The ruling is that if the agent who performs the sarf or salam contract and his counterparty (the one with whom he made the sarf or salam) separate before taking possession, this contract becomes void. Because the condition for the validity of the sarf contract is that both exchanged items be in possession during the session of contract, and for the salam contract, the condition is that the principal (ra's al-mal) be taken into possession by the seller (muslam ilayh) during the session. So when the agent and the other party separate from the session without possession, the condition for validity is not fulfilled, and so the sarf or salam contract becomes void.
Imam al-Quduri says: The separation of the principal from the session before possession is not considered, because the principal is not the contractor. The one entitled to possession due to the contract is the contractor, and the contractor is the agent. Therefore, the agent's possession of the price in sarf is valid, not the principal's. The agent may be someone with whom rights of the contract are connected, such as an adult or a slave permitted to trade, or someone with whom rights are not connected, such as a minor or a non-permitted slave. The entitlement to possession belongs to the contractor because in sarf, possession is part of the contract and its complement. Therefore, from whomever the sarf contract is issued, possession from that person is valid. And in this case, since the sarf contract was issued from the agent, the agent's possession is valid. And when the agent's possession is valid, his separation from the session is considered. The principal's separation (is not considered).
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in sarf and salam contracts when an agent is involved. The core ruling: if the agent and the counterparty separate from the contract session without taking possession of the exchanged goods, the contract becomes void (batil). This is because the validity of sarf requires that both exchanged items be taken possession of during the session, and salam requires that the principal (advance payment) be taken possession of by the seller during the session. The commentator clarifies that only the agent's separation matters, not the principal's. Why? Because the principal is not the contracting party; the agent is the one who entered into the contract. Therefore, the right to take possession lies with the agent, even if the agent is a minor or a restricted slave (whose legal actions are limited but their possession in this context is valid for the contract). The passage contrasts this with the case of a messenger (rasul). A messenger is simply a conveyer of speech; he does not act as a contractor. The contract is formed between the sender and the other party. Thus, if a messenger separates without possession, it is the messenger's separation, but the possession must be taken by the sender. The messenger's possession is not considered that of the contractor, so the contract would not be void due to his separation? Actually, the text says if a messenger separates, it is similar? The text states: 'Unlike the two messengers, because the messengership is for the contract, not for possession, and his speech transfers to the sender. So the possession of the messenger becomes the possession of one who is not the contractor, so it is not valid.' This means that if a messenger is involved, his possession is not considered valid as the contractor's possession; the contractor is the sender. So the ruling for a messenger is that his separation before possession might not affect the contract? Actually, the comparison is: for an agent, his possession is valid, so his separation voids the contract; for a messenger, his possession is not valid (since he is not the contractor), so the contract may remain valid? The text does not explicitly state the consequence for the messenger but implies that the contract is not voided by his separation because his possession is irrelevant. The commentary emphasizes that the agent's possession is what matters.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): Agent; the person who directly contracts on behalf of the principal. In this context, the agent is the contracting party.
رسول (rasūl): Messenger; one who transmits the offer and acceptance but is not a party to the contract.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; physical or constructive control over the subject matter.
افتراق (iftirāq): Separation; leaving the contract session.
عاقد (ʿāqid): Contracting party; the person who enters into the contract as a principal party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sarf contract conducted by an agent, if the agent and the counterparty separate from the session without taking possession of the exchanged items, what is the status of the contract?
A) The contract remains valid because the principal can take possession later.
B) The contract becomes void because the agent's separation before possession violates a condition of validity.
C) The contract becomes void only if the principal also separates.
D) The contract remains valid because possession can be taken after separation.

Key Takeaway
In sarf and salam contracts with an agent, the agent's separation before possession voids the contract; the principal's role is irrelevant, and a messenger's separation does not have the same effect.

Salam Contract Cannot Be Delegated by Muslam Ilayh
Explains why muslam ilayh cannot delegate salam contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits the muslam ilayh from appointing an agent for a salam contract and identify the dalil and the principle of non-extendability of exceptions from qiyas.

Core Idea
Salam is an exception to qiyas; exceptions are confined to their text and cannot be extended via agency.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling regarding the salam (forward) contract: the seller (muslam ilayh) cannot delegate the conclusion of the contract to an agent. While salam itself is a concession permitted by hadith despite the general prohibition of selling what is not in one's possession, this concession is strictly limited. The Hanafi jurists argue that extending the permission to agents would violate the principle that textual exceptions cannot be widened through analogical reasoning. Understanding this limitation is crucial for correctly applying salam contracts in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its apparent contradiction
The ruling is that muslam ilayh cannot appoint an agent. This seems to contradict the permissibility of salam itself, as if salam is allowed, why not allow an agent?
The contradiction is resolved by understanding the nature of the exception.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
By qiyas, salam should be invalid because the subject matter is non-existent at the time of contract. This establishes the baseline ruling.
Qiyas here means analogy to the general rule that one cannot sell what one does not possess.
3
Examine the hadith exception
The hadith provides a specific exception: 'The Prophet ﷺ forbade selling what is not in your possession and permitted salam.' This is the textual basis for salam's validity.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is accepted for this ruling.
4
Apply the principle of non-extension
Exceptions proven contrary to qiyas are confined to the text (maqsurun 'ala nassihi). They cannot be extended via qiyas to other cases, including agency. Thus, muslam ilayh must personally accept the contract.
This principle is key in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ بھی عقد سلم قبول کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہو کیونکہ عقد سلم میں مسلم فیہ ( مبیع ) معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد سلم نا جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ لیکن رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نـهـي عـن بـيـع ما ليس عند الانسان ورخص فی السلم کی وجہ سے مفلسوں کی حاجت دور کرنے کیلئے۔ خلاف قیاس عقد مسلم مشروع کیا گیا ہے اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ مور دنص پر منحصر رہتی ہے۔ اس پر دوسرے کو قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا عقد سلم کو خلاف قیاس مسلم الیہ تو قبول کرنے کا مجاز ہے لیکن اس کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
The answer to this is that the requirement of qiyaas is that the muslam ilayh (the seller in salam) should also not be authorized to accept the salam contract, because in the salam contract the subject matter (the sold item) is non-existent, so the salam contract should have been invalid. However, due to the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade selling what is not in one's possession and permitted salam' – to fulfill the need of the poor – the salam contract was legislated contrary to qiyaas. And something proven by text in opposition to qiyaas remains confined to the text. It is not correct to apply qiyaas to something else. Therefore, the muslam ilayh is authorized to accept the salam contract contrary to qiyaas, but it is not permissible for him to appoint an agent.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling that the seller in a salam contract (muslam ilayh) cannot appoint an agent to conclude the salam contract. The author explains that by analogy (qiyaas), salam contracts would be invalid because the subject matter is non-existent at the time of contract. However, due to a specific hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitting salam to alleviate the needs of the poor, it is legislated as an exception to qiyaas. Such an exception is confined to the text and cannot be extended further. Therefore, while the muslam ilayh himself may conclude a salam contract, he cannot delegate this authority to an agent, as that would be an extension beyond the textual permission.

Key Terms
مسلم الیہ (muslam ilayh): The seller in a salam contract, who undertakes to deliver the specified commodity in the future.
عقد سلم (aql salam): A forward contract where the price is paid in advance for specified goods to be delivered later.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning applied to derive rulings for new cases from established ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the muslam ilayh not appoint an agent for a salam contract according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because salam contracts are inherently invalid
B) Because the hadith allowing salam is a specific exception that cannot be extended via qiyas
C) Because agents are not allowed in any contracts
D) Because the muslam ilayh must be present in person for the contract

Key Takeaway
The muslam ilayh cannot delegate the salam contract because textual exceptions to qiyas are strictly confined to their original scope.

Agent's Separation Before Possession in Sarf and Salam
Ruling with proof on separation before possession for agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separation before possession in sarf/salam contracts conducted by an agent and distinguish the legal effect of an agent versus a messenger.

Core Idea
Possession in the council is a condition for sarf/salam; agent's separation invalidates, but principal's does not.

This passage explores a critical condition for the validity of currency exchange (sarf) and forward sale (salam) contracts: possession must occur in the same council before the parties separate. When an agent conducts the contract, his separation from the counterparty invalidates it, even if the principal remains. A messenger, however, cannot take valid possession because he is not the contracting party. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying Hanafi contract law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts and the ruling
First, note the contracts discussed: sarf (exchange of currencies) and salam (forward sale). The ruling given: if the contracting parties separate from the council before possession is completed, the contract becomes invalid (batil).
This is a condition for validity, not merely a recommendation.
2
Determine who is the contracting party in an agency
In Hanafi law, the agent (wakeel) is the direct party to the contract. He acts in his own name, not as a mere transmitter. Therefore, his possession is the relevant one; the principal's presence or separation does not affect validity.
The agent must be the one to take possession, even if he is a child or a restricted slave.
3
Contrast with a messenger (rasool)
A messenger only conveys the offer and acceptance. His speech transfers to the sender, making the sender the actual contracting party. Consequently, the messenger's possession is not valid—the principal must take possession himself.
The distinguishing factor: the messenger is not a party to the contract; the agent is.
4
Apply the distinction to a scenario
Consider a sarf contract: if the agent leaves before receiving the counter-currency, the contract is void. If the agent's principal leaves but the agent remains, the contract remains valid—only the agent's separation matters.
This shows why the agent's role is pivotal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان فارق الوكيل صاحبه قبل القبض بطل العقد لوجود الافتراق من غير قبض ولا يعتبر مفارقة المؤكل لانه ليس بعاقد والمستحق بالعقد قبض العاقد وهو الوكيل فيصح قبضه وان كان لا يتعلق به الحقوق كالصبي والعبد المحجور عليه بخلاف الرسولين لان الرسالة فى العقد لا فى القبض وينتقل كلامه الى المرسل فصار قبض الرسول قبض غير العاقد فلم يصح
ترجمہ. پس اگر وکیل قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اپنے ساتھی سے جدا ہو گیا تو عقد باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ بغیر قبضہ کے جدا ہونا پایا گیا اور مؤکل کا جدا ہونا معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ موکل عقد کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور عقد کی وجہ سے قبضہ کا مستحق عاقد ہوتا ہے اور وہ وکیل ہے پس وکیل ہی کا قبضہ صحیح ہوگا۔ اگر چہ اس کے ساتھ حقوق متعلق نہ ہوتے ہوں جیسے بچ اور غیر مازون، غلام، برخلاف ایلچیوں کے اسلئے کہ انیچی کرنا عقد کرنے کیلئے ہے نہ کہ قبضہ کرنے کیلئے اور ایچی کا کلام بھیجنے والے کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس چونکہ پیچی کا قبضہ کرنا غیر عاقد کا قبضہ کرنا ہوا۔ اسلئے یہ قبضہ صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عقد صرف یا عقد سلم کرنے والا وکیل اور اس کا وہ ساتھی جس نے اس کے ساتھ عقد صرف یا عقد سلم کیا ہے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے دونوں جدا ہو گئے تو یہ عقد باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عقد صرف کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس عقد میں دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ متفق ہو جائے اور عقد سلم درست ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس عقد میں رأس المال پر مسلم الیہ کا قبضہ تحقیق ہو جائے۔ پس جب وکیل اور دوسرا عاقد قبضہ کیلئے بغیر مجلس سے جدا ہو گئے تو عقد صرف اور عقد سلم کے صحیح ہونے کی شرط نہیں پائی گئی اور جب شرط صحت نہیں پائی گئی تو عقد صرف اور عقد سلم باطل ہو جائے گا۔
صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مجلس عقد سے مؤکل کے جدا ہونے کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ موکل عاقد نہیں ہوتا اور عقد کی وجہ سے قبضہ کا سحق عاقد ہوتا ہے اور عاقد وکیل ہے۔ لہذا بدل صرف پر وکیل کا قبضہ صحیح ہوگا۔ نہ کہ مؤکل کا وکیل خواہ ان لوگوں میں سے ہو جن کے ساتھ حقوق عقد متعلق ہوتے ہیں۔ جیسے بالغ ، عبد ماذون لہ فی التجارہ۔ خواہ ان لوگوں میں سے ہو جن کے ساتھ حقوق عقد متعلق نہیں ہوتے جیسے نابالغ اور عبد غیر مازون لہ اور قبضہ کا مستحق عاقد اسلئے ہوتا ہے کہ عقد صرف میں قبضہ عقد کا اور عبد غیر ماذون لۂ تمہ اور تکملہ ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا جس سے عقد صرف صادر ہو گا اس کی طرف سے قبضہ بھی صحیح ہوگا اور مذکورہ صورت میں چونکہ عقد صرف وکیل سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے قبضہ بھی وکیل کا صحیح ہوگا اور جب قبضہ وکیل کا صحیح ہے تو مجلس عقد سے اس کا جدا ہونا معتبر ہوگا۔ مؤکل کا جدا ہونا

معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کسی نے عقد صرف یا عقد سلم منعقد کرنے کیلئے کسی کو اچھی بنادیا تو بدل صرف پرا پیچی کا قبضہ کرنا صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ چنانچہ ایچی کے قبضہ کرنے سے عقد صرف درست نہ ہوگا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ اینچی صرف عقد منعقد کرنے کے واسطے مقرر کیا گیا ہے نہ کہ قبضہ کرنے کے واسطے۔ اور جب یہ بات ہے تو ایلچی کا کلام ، مرسل ( بھیجنے والے) کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا اور جب ایچی کا کلام مرسل کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا تو عاقد مرسل ہوگا نہ کہ اینچی اور جب عاقد مرسل ہوانہ کہ ایچی تو عاقد یعنی مرسل کا قبضہ صحیح ہوگا۔ اور بیچی جو غیر عاقد ہے اس کا قبضہ صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
If the agent separates from his companion before taking possession, the contract is invalid because separation occurs without possession. The separation of the principal is not considered because he is not the contracting party. The one entitled to possession by the contract is the contracting party, and he is the agent, so his possession is valid even if rights are not attached to him, like a child or a slave under interdiction. Unlike messengers, because the mission is for the contract, not for possession, and his speech transfers to the sender, so the messenger's possession becomes possession of a non-contracting party, thus invalid.
[Translation of the Urdu commentary as given in the text]
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of separation before possession in sarf (currency exchange) and salam (forward sale) contracts when conducted by an agent (wakeel). The ruling: if the agent and the other party separate from the contract council before taking possession, the contract becomes invalid. This is because for sarf, mutual possession of both currencies in the council is a condition for validity; for salam, possession of the capital in the council is a condition. The separation of the principal (muwakkil) is irrelevant because he is not the contracting party; the agent is the direct party. However, a messenger (rasool) is different: his role is only to transmit the contract, not to take possession, so his possession is ineffective. The text also notes that the agent's possession is valid even if he is a child or a restricted slave (who cannot own rights), because possession is purely physical. This distinction between an agent (who acts on his own behalf) and a messenger (who merely conveys the contract) is crucial in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakeel): An agent authorized to conclude a contract on behalf of another; he is the direct contracting party.
رسول (rasool): A messenger who conveys the contract offer/acceptance; he does not act as a party.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking control of the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sarf contract conducted by an agent, what happens if the agent and the other party leave the council before taking possession?
A) The contract is valid if the principal later takes possession.
B) The contract is invalid because possession must occur in the council.
C) The contract is suspended until possession is taken.
D) The agent can take possession later and the contract becomes valid.

Key Takeaway
In sarf and salam, possession in the council is a condition for validity; only the contracting party's separation matters, not the principal's, and a messenger cannot validly take possession.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Agent Reimbursement for Paying Price from Own Money
Ruling and reasoning for agent's reimbursement with virtual exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent's right to reimbursement and explain the rationale of virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya).

Core Idea
When an agent pays the price from his own money, a virtual exchange entitles him to reclaim it from the principal.

A purchasing agent (wakeel bil-shira') sometimes pays the price from his own pocket before seeking reimbursement from the principal (muwakkil). This lesson clarifies that such payment is not a gift or loan; rather, Islamic law recognizes a virtual exchange between agent and principal, granting the agent a right to reclaim the amount. We will explore the evidence from mutual oaths and the right to return for defect, and note the consensus among the four Sunni schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize the key elements: an agent authorized to buy, pays the price from his own money, takes possession of the item, and delivers it to the principal.
2
State the Ruling
The agent has the right (ja'iz) to reclaim the price from the principal. This is not tabarru' (gift).
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand Virtual Exchange (Mubadala Hukmiyya)
The relationship is treated as a virtual sale: the agent acts like a seller, the principal like a buyer. This concept is the basis for reimbursement.
The witness for this virtual exchange is that the parties take oaths if they dispute the price, and the principal can return the item for defect.
4
Note the Consensus
Imams Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad all agree on this ruling, as mentioned in the commentary.
No inter-madhhab dispute exists on this specific point.
5
Apply to Dispute Resolution
If the agent and principal disagree on the amount, each swears an oath (as in a real sale). The principal may also reject the item due to defect and return it to the agent.
These consequences affirm the virtual exchange model.

مبیع دے چکا ہے تو وکیل کو موکل سے مذکورہ پلیچ کاشن لینے کا اختیار بھی حاصل ہوگا۔
He (al-Quduri) said: 'And if the agent for purchase pays the price from his own money and takes possession of the purchased item, then he has the right to reclaim it from the principal because a virtual exchange has been established between them. For this reason, if they differ regarding the price, they both take an oath, and the principal can return the purchased item to the agent due to a defect, and the purchased item has been delivered to the principal from the agent, so he can reclaim the price from him. And because the rights pertain to the agent, and the principal is aware of this, so he is content with the payment from the agent's money.' [Then Urdu translation and commentary extending the reasoning and mentioning that Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad are of this opinion.]
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on an agent for purchase (wakeel bil-shira') who pays the purchase price from his own money and takes possession of the purchased item. The ruling: the agent has the right to reclaim that amount from the principal (muwakkil). This is not considered a gift (tabarru') from the agent. The reasoning is that a virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya) is established between the agent and the principal: the agent acts like a seller and the principal like a buyer. Evidence for this virtual exchange includes: (1) if they dispute the price, they both take oaths (like buyer and seller in a real sale), and (2) if the principal finds a defect, he can return the item to the agent (as a buyer returns to a seller). The commentary further notes that Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad also hold this view, though the Hanafi position is supported by the reasoning of virtual exchange. The passage emphasizes that because the agent has delivered the item to the principal under this virtual exchange, he can claim reimbursement.

Key Terms
وکیل بالشراء (wakeel bil-shira'): An agent authorized to purchase an item on behalf of the principal.
مبادلہ حکمی (mubadala hukmiyya): A virtual exchange that is treated like a real sale for legal purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the agent have the right to reclaim the price from the principal when he pays from his own money?
A) Because the agent is merely a guarantor
B) Because a virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya) is established between them
C) Because the principal is legally obliged to pay the agent immediately
D) Because the agent is considered the owner of the purchased item

Key Takeaway
The agent's payment is not a gift; a virtual exchange allows him to reclaim the price from the principal.

Agent Reimbursement When Paying from Personal Funds
Ruling and proofs for agent's right to reclaim price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent's right to reclaim the price paid from his own funds, and explain the two proofs: constructive exchange and implied permission.

Core Idea
An agent who pays from his own pocket is not a donor; a constructive exchange gives him the right to reclaim.

When an agent for purchase pays the price from his own money and takes delivery, does he have any right to recover that amount from his client? This lesson clarifies that the agent is not making a donation; rather, a constructive exchange (mubādala ḥukmiyya) is deemed to occur, granting him the right of reimbursement. We will examine the ruling and its proofs as presented in the Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Locate the main ruling: the agent who pays the price from his own funds and takes possession may reclaim the price from the client. Identify the conditions: agent pays from own money, takes possession of the item.
The ruling applies to the wakīl bil-shirā (agent for purchase).
2
Understand the first proof: constructive exchange (mubādala ḥukmiyya)
The text argues that a constructive exchange exists between agent and client, making the agent like a seller and the client like a buyer. Evidence: if they dispute the price, both take oaths; and the client may return the item for a defect to the agent.
These features are exclusive to contracts of sale.
3
Analyze the second proof: implied permission
The agent is not a donor (mutabarri‘) because the client implicitly permits the payment. Since all rights of the sale revert to the agent and the client knows this, the client is deemed to consent.
Implied permission (dalālat al-ijāza) is sufficient in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Consider the additional rule: destruction of the item
If the purchased item is destroyed in the agent’s possession before he detains it for his price, it is considered destroyed from the client’s property. The agent’s right to reimbursement remains, and the agent is not liable because his possession is as a trust (amāna).
This reinforces the agent's right to reclaim.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific case (e.g., agent buys a car for client using his own money), determine that the agent can reclaim the price. Then consider a variation: if the client refuses to pay, the agent may detain the item.
If the item is destroyed without detention, the client bears the loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
