معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کسی نے عقد صرف یا عقد سلم منعقد کرنے کیلئے کسی کو وکیل بنایا تو بدل صرف پر اس کا قبضہ کرنا صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ چنانچہ وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے عقد صرف درست نہ ہوگا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل صرف عقد منعقد کرنے کے واسطے مقرر کیا گیا ہے نہ کہ قبضہ کرنے کے واسطے۔ اور جب یہ بات ہے تو وکیل کا کلام، مرسل ( بھیجنے والے) کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا اور جب وکیل کا کلام مرسل کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا تو عاقد مرسل ہوگا نہ کہ وکیل اور جب عاقد مرسل ہوا نہ کہ وکیل تو عاقد یعنی مرسل کا قبضہ صحیح ہوگا۔ اور وکیل جو غیر عاقد ہے اس کا قبضہ صحیح نہ ہوگا۔

وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا اور مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا تو موکل پر رجوع کرے گا

قال واذا دفع الوكيل بالشراء الثمن من ماله وقبض المبيع فله ان يرجع به على المؤكل لانه انعقدت بينهما مبادلة حكمية ولهذا اذا اختلفا في الثمن يتحالفان ويرد المؤكل بالعيب على الوكيل وقد سُلّم المشترى للمؤكل من جهة الوكيل فيرجع عليه ولان الحقوق لما كانت اليه وقد علمه المؤكل فيكون راضيا بدفعه من ماله

ترجمہ اور اگر وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال سے ثمن دے دیا اور مبیع پر قبضہ کرلیا تو وکیل کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ موکل سے ثمن واپس لے۔ اسلئے کہ وکیل اور مؤکل کے درمیان حکما مبادلہ منعقد ہو گیا۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر وکیل اور موکل نے ثمن میں اختلاف کیا تو دونوں قسم کھا ئیں گے اور موکل مبیع عیب کی وجہ سے وکیل کو واپس کرے گا اور وکیل کی طرف سے مؤکل کیلئے مبیع سپرد ہو چکی ہے۔ لہذا وکیل، مؤکل سے اپنا ثمن واپس لے گا۔ اور اس لئے کہ حقوق جب وکیل کی طرف راجع ہیں اور مؤکل اس کو جانتا بھی ہے تو موکل ثمن وکیل کے مال سے دینے پر راضی ہوگا۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال میں سے ثمن ادا کر کے مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا تو ثمن کا ادا کرنا اس کی طرف سے تبرع نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ وکیل مذکورہ ثمن مؤکل سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان حکما مبادلہ ہے اس طور پر کہ وکیل بائع کے مانند ہے اور مؤکل مشتری کے مانند ہے اور مبادلہ حکمی کی علامت یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل اور مؤکل کے درمیان مقدار ثمن میں اختلاف ہو گیا تو ان دونوں سے قسم لی جاتی ہے اور تخالف فریقین سے قسم لینا مبادلہ کے خواص میں سے ہے۔ چنانچہ بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان اگر مقدار ثمن میں اختلاف ہو جائے اور دونوں کے پاس بینہ نہ ہو تو دونوں سے قسم لی جائے گی۔ اگر کسی نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو اس کے خلاف فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اگر دونوں قسم کھا گئے تو قاضی اس بیع کو فسخ کر دے گا۔ بہر حال اس مسئلہ میں وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان مقدار ثمن میں اختلاف کی صورت میں دونوں سے قسم لینا اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان حکما مبادلہ منعقد ہوا ہے اور اگر مؤکل مبیع کے کسی عیب پر مطلع ہو تو وہ اس عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع وکیل کی طرف واپس کر سکتا ہے اور عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع واپس کرنا یہ بھی مبادلہ کے خواص میں سے ہے۔ بہر حال وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان مبادلہ حکمی پایا گیا اور اس مبادلہ کے تحت وکیل مؤکل کو مبیع سپرد کر چکا ہے۔ پس جب مبادلہ کے تحت وکیل، مؤکل کو مبیع دے چکا ہے تو وکیل کو موکل سے مذکورہ ثمن لینے کا اختیار بھی حاصل ہوگا۔

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل ثمن ادا کرنے میں متبرع اس وقت ہوتا جبکہ یہ ثمن موکل کی اجازت کے بغیر ادا کیا گیا ہوتا۔ حالانکہ ثمن مؤکل کی اجازت سے ادا کیا گیا ہے۔ اگر چہ مؤکل کی اجازت دلالۃً پائی گئی اور مؤکل کی اجازت دلالۃً اسلئے پائی گئی کہ بیع کے جملہ حقوق وکیل کی طرف راجع ہوتے ہیں اور موکل کو اس کا علم بھی ہے پس جب بیع کے حقوق وکیل کی طرف راجع ہوتے ہیں تو ثمن کا مطالبہ وکیل ہی سے ہوگا اور جب ثمن کا مطالبہ وکیل سے ہوگا اور مؤکل کو اس کا علم ہے تو گویا موکل اس بات پر راضی ہو گیا کہ وکیل اپنے مال میں سے ثمن ادا کر دے اور مؤکل کا اس بات پر راضی ہونا گویا موکل کی اجازت ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ وکیل نے اپنے مال میں سے جو ثمن ادا کیا ہے وہ مؤکل کی اجازت سے ادا کیا ہے اور جب مؤکل کی اجازت سے ادا کیا ہے تو وکیل، موکل پر تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور جب وکیل تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہے تو اس کو موکل سے رجوع کرنے کا پورا پورا اختیار حاصل ہوگا۔ حتی کہ اگر مؤکل ثمن دینے میں چوں چرا کرے تو وکیل کو مبیع اپنے پاس روک لینے کا اختیار ہے۔

اگر مبیع وکیل کے ہاتھ میں روکنے سے پہلے ہلاک ہو گئی تو موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی

فان هلك المبيع في يده قبل حبسه هلك من مال المؤكل ولم يسقط الثمن لان يده كيد المؤكل فاذا لم يحبسه يصير المؤكل قابضا بيده

ترجمہ۔ پس اگر وکیل کے قبضہ میں مبیع ہلاک ہوگئی وکیل کے اس کو روکنے سے پہلے تو وہ موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی اور ثمن ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ، وکیل کا قبضہ مؤکل کے قبضہ کے مانند ہے۔ پس جب وکیل نے اس کو نہیں روکا تو موکل وکیل کے قبضہ سے قابض ہو جائے گا۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال میں سے ثمن ادا کر کے مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا اور مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہو گئی۔ حالانکہ وکیل نے ثمن کی وجہ سے مبیع اپنے پاس روکی بھی نہیں تھی تو یہ مبیع مؤکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی یعنی مؤکل کا مال تلف ہوا نہ کہ وکیل کا۔ حتی کہ ثمن مؤکل کے ذمہ سے ساقط نہ ہوگا اور وکیل کا حق رجوع باطل نہ ہوگا بلکہ وکیل کو مؤکل سے اپنا ثمن واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔

دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کا مبیع پر قبضہ ایسا ہے جیسے موکل کا۔ پس جب وکیل نے اپنے ثمن کی وجہ سے مبیع کو نہیں روکا تو وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے حکما مؤکل قابض ہو جائے گا اور وکیل کے قبضہ میں مبیع کا ہلاک ہونا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ موکل کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہونا اور موکل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل کا حق رجوع ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کا موکل سے رجوع بالثمن کا اختیار ساقط نہ ہوگا۔

علامہ بدرالدین عینی نے عینی شرح ہدایہ میں ایک دلیل یہ تحریر فرمائی کہ مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ میں امانت ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے مبیع پر اپنے لئے قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ بلکہ موکل کی اجازت سے مؤکل کیلئے قبضہ کیا ہے۔ اور جب مؤکل کی اجازت سے مؤکل کیلئے قبضہ کیا ہے تو یہ قبضہ بطور امانت ہوگا۔ اور بغیر تعدی امانت کے ہلاک ہونے سے امین پر چونکہ تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اسلئے اس مسئلہ میں بھی وکیل پر کوئی تاوان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب امین ہونے کی وجہ سے وکیل پر کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا تو وکیل نے جو ثمن بائع کو دیا ہے وہ وکیل وہ
And when the agent for purchase pays the price from his own wealth and takes possession of the purchased item, he may claim it back from the client because a constructive exchange (mubādala ḥukmiyya) is concluded between them. For this reason, if they differ about the price, they both take an oath; and the client returns the purchased item to the agent due to a defect; and the purchased item has been delivered to the client from the agent, so he claims from him. And because the rights are directed to him (the agent) and the client knows that, so he is content with his paying it from his own wealth.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding an agent for purchase (wakīl bil-shirā) who pays the purchase price from his own funds and takes possession of the bought item. The ruling: he has the right to reclaim that amount from his client (muwakkil). The text provides two main proofs: First, a constructive exchange (mubādala ḥukmiyya) is deemed to occur between agent and client, making the agent analogous to a seller and the client to a buyer. Evidence of this constructive exchange is that if they dispute the price, they both take oaths—a feature of real sales; also, the client can return the item for a defect to the agent, another feature of sales. Second, the agent is not a donor (mutabarri‘) because the client implicitly permits the payment, since all rights of the sale revert to the agent and the client knows this, implying consent. The text also states that this view is held by Imam Malik, Imam Shafi‘i, and Imam Ahmad, indicating broad agreement. Additionally, if the purchased item is destroyed in the agent’s possession before he detains it for his price, it is considered destroyed from the client’s property, and the agent’s right to reimbursement remains. The commentary by Badr al-Din al-‘Ayni adds that the agent’s possession is as a trust (amāna), so no compensation is due from him if it is destroyed without negligence.

Key Terms
وكيل بالشراء (wakīl bil-shirā): An agent appointed specifically to purchase an item on behalf of the client.
مبادلة حكمية (mubādala ḥukmiyya): A constructive exchange deemed to exist between agent and client for the purpose of legal rulings, treating the agent as seller and client as buyer.
موكل (muwakkil): The person who appoints the agent (principal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an agent for purchase pays the price from his own money and takes possession of the item, what is the ruling on his right to reimbursement?
A) He cannot reclaim because he paid voluntarily.
B) He can reclaim the price from the client because a constructive exchange occurs.
C) He can only reclaim if the client explicitly permitted.
D) He can reclaim only if the item is destroyed in his possession.

Key Takeaway
An agent who pays from his own funds and takes possession may reclaim the price from his client due to the constructive exchange and implied permission.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Wakil's Right to Detain Goods: Abu Hanifa vs. Zufar
Hanafi ruling on wakil's detention right with rebuttal of Zufar's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position from Zufar's regarding the wakil's right to detain purchased goods and explain the two Hanafi responses.

Core Idea
The wakil is constructively the seller — he can detain goods until paid, despite Zufar's objection.

In this passage, we explore a key intra-Hanafi disagreement. Al-Quduri states that the wakil (purchase agent) has the right to detain the purchased goods until he receives payment from the principal. Imam Zufar objects, arguing that the principal's constructive possession extinguishes this right. The Hanafi school provides two robust responses rooted in the concepts of involuntary possession and suspended possession (qabḍ mawqūf). This dispute also aligns with broader inter-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim and its basis
Recognize that Al-Quduri asserts the wakil's right to detain purchased goods before receiving payment. The basis is that the wakil is constructively (ḥukman) in the position of a seller (bā'i') in relation to the principal as buyer.
This analogy is drawn from the general rule that a seller may detain goods until payment.
2
State Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that the principal becomes a constructive possessor the moment the wakil takes possession, as if the goods have been delivered. Therefore, the wakil's right to detain drops.
Zufar's view aligns with other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali).
3
Analyze the first Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the principal's constructive possession is involuntary and unavoidable; legally, such possession is pardoned and treated as non-existent. Hence, the wakil is not deemed to have waived his right.
Key principle: involuntary matters are overlooked in law (al-umūr al-qasriyya tu'fā).
4
Analyze the second Hanafi response
The second response denies that the principal becomes possessor at all. Instead, the wakil's possession is suspended (mawqūf): if he detains, it is for himself; if he does not, it is for the principal. Thus, until he decides, the principal is not a possessor.
This doctrine of suspended possession is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a Hanafi court, the wakil may lawfully withhold the goods; in a Shafi'i or Maliki court, he must deliver them immediately.
The difference directly affects the wakil's security for his payment.

غیر اختیاری چیز ہے۔ جس سے بچنا ممکن نہیں۔ اور جو چیز غیر اختیاری طور پر ثابت ہو اور اس سے بچنا ممکن نہ ہو اس کو شرعا عفو قرار دیا جاتا ہے اور وہ عدم کے حکم میں ہوتی ہے۔ پس جب وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے موکل کا قابض ہونا عدم کے حکم میں ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل نہیں ہوگا کہ وکیل اپنے حق حبس کو ساقط کرنے پر راضی ہے اور جب وکیل اپنا حق حبس ساقط کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہے تو وکیل کا حق حبس ساقط نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس کا ثمن وصول ہونے تک کیلئے مبیع روکنے کا پورا حق ہوگا على ان قبضه...... الخ سے دوسرا جواب ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے مؤکل حکما قابض ہو جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ ابتداء میں وکیل کا قبضہ موقوف ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر وکیل نے مبیع کو اپنے پاس نہ روکا تو یہ قبضہ موکل کیلئے واقع ہو گا اور اگر وکیل نے مبیع کو اپنے پاس روک لیا تو یہ قبضہ خود وکیل کیلئے واقع ہوگا۔ پس جب وکیل کا قبضہ ابتدا میں موقوف اور متردد ہے تو وکیل کے قبضہ سے مؤکل قابض نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب وکیل کے قبضہ سے مؤکل قابض نہ ہوا تو وکیل کا حق حبس بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا۔
He (the wakil) has the right to detain it until payment of the price because we have explained that he is in the position of the seller from the principal. Zufar said: He does not have that because the principal becomes a possessor by his (wakil's) hand, so it is as if he handed it over to him, thus the right of detention drops. We said: This is something unavoidable, so he is not considered agree to waive his right of detention. Moreover, his possession is suspended: if he does not detain it, it is for the principal; if he detains it, it is for himself. Translation: The wakil has the option to detain the goods until he receives his price. This is due to the evidence we mentioned that the wakil is like the seller in relation to the principal. Imam Zufar said: He does not have this right because the principal becomes a possessor by the wakil's taking possession, so it is as if the wakil has delivered the goods to the principal. Therefore, the right of detention drops. We answer: This is something unavoidable, so the wakil is not regarded as consenting to waive his right of detention. Additionally, the wakil's possession is suspended: if he does not detain the goods, it is for the principal; if he detains them, it is for himself. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the wakil can detain the goods before receiving the price, whether he gave the price to the seller or not. In any case, the wakil is permitted to detain the goods to collect the price from the principal. The evidence is that between the wakil and the principal there is a constructive sale: the wakil by purchase is constructively the seller and the principal is the buyer. It has passed in Kitab al-Buyu' that the seller has the right to detain the goods before receiving the price. Hence, here too, the wakil, who is constructively the seller, has the right to detain the goods before receiving the price. Imam Zufar said: The wakil has no right to detain the goods. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad agree with him. (Mini) Imam Zufar's evidence is that by the wakil's possession of the goods, the principal becomes constructively a possessor, and it is as if the wakil has delivered the goods to the principal. When the wakil has delivered, his right of detention drops. Because if the goods had actually come into the principal's possession, the wakil would have no right of detention. Similarly, when the goods constructively come into the principal's possession, the wakil's right of detention drops. But we have two answers: The first answer is that the principal's constructive possession by the wakil's possession is an involuntary matter from which avoidance is impossible. And something that is established involuntarily and unavoidable is considered legally pardoned and is treated as non-existent. So when the principal's possession due to the wakil's possession is treated as non-existent, it does not indicate that the wakil consents to waive his right of detention. And when the wakil does not consent to waive his right, his right of detention does not drop; rather he has a full right to detain the goods until he receives the price. The second answer from 'ala anna qabdahu... is that we do not concede that the principal becomes constructively a possessor by the wakil's possession. Rather, initially the wakil's possession is suspended: if the wakil does not detain the goods, the possession is for the principal; if the wakil detains the goods, the possession is for the wakil himself. Since the wakil's possession is initially suspended and ambiguous, the principal does not become a possessor by the wakil's possession. And when the principal does not become a possessor, the wakil's right of detention does not drop.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar regarding the right of an agent (wakil) to detain purchased goods (mabi') until he receives the price (thaman) from the principal (muwakkil). The author, following Al-Quduri, states that the wakil has the right to detain the goods before receiving the price, whether or not the wakil has paid the seller. The evidence is that the wakil is constructively (hukman) in the position of the seller, and the principal is the buyer. Just as a seller can detain the goods until payment, so can the wakil. Imam Zufar objects on the grounds that the principal becomes a possessor (qabid) by the wakil's possession, so it is as if the goods have been delivered, and the right of detention is lost. The Hanafi response gives two answers: First, the principal's constructive possession is involuntary and unavoidable, therefore legally pardoned and treated as non-existent; the wakil does not consent to waive his right. Second, the wakil's possession is initially suspended (mawquf): if he does not detain, it is for the principal; if he detains, it is for himself. Therefore, the principal does not become a possessor merely by the wakil's possession, and the wakil's right of detention remains intact. The passage also notes that other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree with Zufar, but the Hanafi position is the relied-upon one.

Key Terms
وکیل بالشراء (wakīl bi al-shirā'): An agent authorized to purchase goods on behalf of the principal.
حق الحبس (ḥaqq al-ḥabs): The right to detain the sold goods until payment of the price.
قبض موقوف (qabḍ mawqūf): Suspended possession that becomes effective for one party based on subsequent action (detention or non-detention).
حکما (ḥukman): Constructively or legally; in the eyes of the law, not physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true about the wakil's possession before he decides to detain?
A) It is immediately transferred to the principal.
B) It is suspended (mawquf) until the wakil's intention is clear.
C) It is void unless the wakil pays the seller.
D) It is valid only for the principal.

Key Takeaway
The wakil's right to detain goods until payment is affirmed by the Hanafi school through the constructive sale analogy and the doctrine of suspended possession.

The Wakil's Guarantee for Detained Goods Destroyed
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guarantee classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the guarantee when a wakil's detained goods are destroyed, identify the mufta bihi, and apply the correct ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Three Hanafi imams analogize the wakil's guarantee to sale, pledge, or usurpation—the mufta bihi is sale-like, extinguishing the price.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the nature of the guarantee when a wakil (agent) detains purchased goods (mabi') and they are accidentally destroyed. The dispute hinges on whether the wakil is like a seller, a pledge-holder, or a usurper. Understanding this difference is crucial for determining who bears the loss in such transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
List the three positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say sale-like guarantee (price drops), Abu Yusuf says pledge-like guarantee (lesser of value and price), Zufar says usurpation-like guarantee (full value).
2
Understand the analogy of each position
For Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: the wakil is like a seller detaining goods for price; destruction rescinds the sale. For Abu Yusuf: the wakil detains for collection like a pledge-holder; destruction triggers rahn guarantee. For Zufar: detention without right is like usurpation; full value is due.
3
Analyze the evidence for the sale-like position
The Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf: the contract is rescinded between principal and wakil, analogous to a defect return. So the price drops.
This is the Hanafi reply in the text: 'We say: It is rescinded with respect to the principal and the wakil, just as when the principal returns it due to a defect and the wakil is pleased with it.'
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the sale-like view, the principal does not owe the price. Under the pledge-like view, the wakil compensates the lesser of value and price. Under usurpation-like view, the wakil pays full value.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (sale-like), as stated in the text and supported by the Hanafi response.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

فان حبسه فهلک کان مضمونا ضمان الرهن عند ابي يوسف وضمان البيع عند محمد وهو قول أبي حنيفة وضمان الغصب عند زفر لانه منع بغير حق لهما انه بمنزلة البائع منه فكان حبسه لاستيفاء الثمن فيسقط بهلاكه ولابي يوسف انه مضمون بالحبس للاستيفاء بعد ان لم يكن وهو الرهن بعينه بخلاف المبيع لان البيع ينفسخ بهلاكه وههنا لا ينفسخ اصل العقد قلنا ينفسخ فى حق المؤكل والوكيل كما اذا رده المؤكل بعيب ورضى الوكيل به ترجمہ پس اگر وکیل نے مبیع کو روکا پھر وہ ہلاک ہوگئی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ضمان رہن کی طرح مضمون ہو گی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ضمان بیع کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ یہی قول امام ابو حنیفہ کا ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک ضمان غصب کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ اسلئے کہ مبیع ناحق رد کی گئی ہے۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل، موکل کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے والے کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ پس وکیل کا مبیع کو روکنا ثمن وصول کرنے کیلئے ہے۔ لہذا مبیع کے ہلاک ہونے سے ثمن ساقط ہو جائے گا اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مبیع اپنا مال وصول کرنے کیلئے روکنے کی وجہ سے مضمون ہے۔ حالانکہ اب تک مضمون نہ تھی اور بعینہ یہی معنی رہن کے میں برخلاف مبیع کے اسلئے کہ بیع بیع کے ہلاک ہونے سے فسخ ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور یہاں اصل عقد فسخ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ مؤکل اور وکیل کے حق میں عقد فسخ ہو جاتا ہے جیسا کہ جب مؤکل اس کو عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کرے اور وکیل اس پر راضی ہو جائے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے موکل سے ثمن وصول کرنے کے خاطر مبیع کو اپنے پاس روک لیا اور مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہوگئی تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مبیع شی مرہونہ کی طرح مضمون ہوگی۔ یعنی جس طرح شی مرہونہ ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں قیمت اور دین میں سے جو کم ہوتا ہے اس کے ساتھ مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ مثلا شی مرہونہ کی قیمت پچاس روپیہ ہے اور مرتہن کا راہن کے ذمہ دین (قرضہ) ساٹھ روپیہ ہے تو شی مرہونہ قیمت کے ساتھ مضمون ہوگی۔ یعنی پچاس روپیہ کا مرتہن پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اور چونکہ مرتہن کا راہن کے ذمہ ساٹھ روپیہ قرض ہے۔ اسلئے ان میں سے پچاس تاوان کے منہا کرنے کے بعد مرتہن راہن سے دس روپیہ واپس لے گا اور اگر شی مرہونہ کی قیمت ساٹھ روپیہ ہو اور راہن کے ذمہ دین پچاس روپیہ ہوں تو شی مرہونہ دین کے ساتھ مضمون ہوگی یعنی شی مرہونہ کے تاوان میں راہن کے ذمہ سے مرتہن کا دین ساقط ہو جائے گا اور راہن کو مرتہن سے مزید کسی رقم کے مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باقی دس روپیہ کی مقدار مرتہن کے پاس امانت ہے اور امانت کا کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا اسلئے مرتہن پر دس روپیہ کا تاوان واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح مذکورہ مسئلہ میں وکیل کے قبضہ سے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں مبیع قیمت اور ثمن میں سے جو کم ہو گا اس کے ساتھ مضمون
If he detains it and it perishes, it is guaranteed: according to Abu Yusuf, with the guarantee of a pledge (rahn); according to Muhammad, with the guarantee of a sale (bay' ) – and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa; and according to Zufar, with the guarantee of usurpation (ghasb) because he prevented it without right. Their (Muhammad and Abu Hanifa's) evidence: He is in the position of the seller from him, so his detention is for collecting the price, and [the price] drops by its destruction. Abu Yusuf's evidence: It is guaranteed due to detention for collection after it was not [guaranteed], and this is exactly the meaning of a pledge, unlike a sale because the sale is rescinded by its destruction, whereas here the original contract is not rescinded. We say: It is rescinded with respect to the principal and the wakil, just as when the principal returns it due to a defect and the wakil is pleased with it. Translation: If the wakil detains the goods and they are destroyed, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is guaranteed like a pledge (daman al-rahn). According to Imam Muhammad, it is guaranteed like a sale (daman al-bay') – and this is also the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Imam Zufar, it is guaranteed like usurpation (daman al-ghasb) because the goods were wrongfully withheld. The evidence of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the wakil is in the position of the seller to the principal, so his detention is to collect the price, and therefore the price drops by the destruction. Abu Yusuf's evidence is that the goods are guaranteed due to detention for collection after they were not guaranteed, and this is exactly the meaning of a pledge, unlike a sale because a sale is rescinded by destruction, whereas here the original contract is not rescinded. We (the Hanafis) respond: It is rescinded with respect to the principal and the wakil, just as when the principal returns it due to a defect and the wakil is pleased with it. Explanation: The case is that if the wakil bil-shira' detains the goods to collect the price from the principal, and the goods are destroyed in the wakil's possession, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the goods are guaranteed like a pledged item. That is, like a pledged item, when destroyed, the guarantee is with the lesser of the value and the debt. For example, if the value of the pledge is fifty rupees and the creditor's debt from the debtor is sixty rupees, the pledge is guaranteed with its value, so fifty rupees is wajib as compensation on the creditor. Since the debtor owed sixty, after deducting fifty as compensation, the creditor takes back ten rupees from the debtor. If the value is sixty and the debt is fifty, the pledge is guaranteed with the debt, so the debt is dropped and the debtor has no further claim. The remaining ten rupees value is an amanah (trust) with the creditor, and no compensation is due for a trust. Similarly, in the mentioned case, when the mabi' is destroyed in the wakil's possession, it is guaranteed with the lesser of the value and the price (thaman).
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of the guarantee (daman) when the wakil detains the mabi' (purchased goods) and they are accidentally destroyed in his possession. Three positions are presented: (1) Abu Yusuf: It is like a pledge (rahn) – the wakil is like a creditor retaining a pledge, and upon destruction, the guarantee is the lesser of the value and the debt (here, the price). (2) Muhammad (and Abu Hanifa): It is like a sale (bay') – the wakil is like a seller who detained the goods, and if they perish, the price drops (i.e., the principal's obligation to pay is extinguished). The Hanafi response (from the text) to Abu Yusuf's argument is that the original contract is not rescinded in a sale generally, but here it is rescinded with respect to the principal and wakil, analogous to when the principal returns defective goods and the wakil agrees. (3) Zufar: It is like usurpation (ghasb) – the wakil wrongfully withheld the goods, so he is liable for full value. The passage then explains Abu Yusuf's view with an example: if the goods are worth less than the price, the wakil compensates the value; if more, the price drops and the excess is amanah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa: the price drops (sale-like), because the wakil's detention is lawful and analogous to a seller's detention.

Key Terms
مضمون (maḍmūn): Guaranteed; subject to compensation (daman) if destroyed.
ضمان الرهن (ḍamān al-rahn): The guarantee of a pledge: compensation is the lesser of the value and the debt.
فسخ العقد (faskh al-'aqd): Rescission of the contract; here, the purchase contract between principal and wakil is rescinded upon destruction of goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, if the wakil detains the mabi' and it is destroyed, what happens to the price (thaman) owed by the principal?
A) The price remains due in full.
B) The price drops and is no longer owed.
C) The wakil must pay the principal the lesser of the value and the price.
D) The wakil must pay the full value of the goods.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position treats the wakil's detention as analogous to a seller's detention, so the price drops upon destruction.

Guarantee of Destroyed Mabi' After Agent's Detention: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman after detention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on guarantee when a purchasing agent detains the mabi' and it is destroyed, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each position.

Core Idea
Three different qiyas give three different liability rules for the same loss.

When an agent detains the purchased item to secure payment, his possession changes from trust to something else. The Hanafi imams disagree on the nature of that change. This lesson unpacks their analogies and the practical differences in who pays whom when the item is destroyed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key act and the dispute
The act: purchasing agent detains mabi' after purchase to collect thaman from principal; mabi' is then destroyed without fault. The dispute: what guarantee (daman) applies?
Note that before detention, destruction is on principal (amanah).
2
State each imam's analogy and ruling
Abu Hanifa & Muhammad (the two parties): qiyas to sale → thaman canceled from principal. Abu Yusuf: qiyas to pledge → set-off between thaman and compensation. Zufar: qiyas to usurpation → set-off with full value/like.
The analogy determines the result.
3
Work through numeric examples
Take the example: thaman 15, value 10. Under each analogy, compute the final payment or receipt between agent and principal.
This shows the thamarah al-khilaf clearly.
4
Analyze the objection and answer against the two parties
Objection: if agent is like seller, why does guarantee only apply after detention? Answer: detention indicates agent took possession for himself, making him a seller; without detention, he is a trustee.
This refines the analogy.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text favors Abu Yusuf's view (author of al-Hidayah refutes the two parties). However, later fuqaha may follow the two parties or Zufar in different contexts.
No final tarjih is given.

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة

ہوگی۔ مثلا وکیل بالشراء نے بائع سے پندرہ روپیہ من پر معاملہ کیا ہے اور ہلاک شدہ مبیع کی قیمت دس روپیہ ہے تو مبیع قیمت کے ساتھ مضمون ہو گی۔ یعنی موکل کے ذمہ میں وکیل کے لئے ثمن یعنی پندرہ روپیہ واجب ہیں، اور موکل کے لئے وکیل پر مبیع کا تاوان دس روپیہ واجب ہیں تو ثمن میں سے تاوان کے دس روپیہ منہا کرنے کے بعد وکیل موکل سے پانچ روپیہ واپس لے گا۔ اور اگر ثمن دس روپیہ ہوں اور مبیع کی قیمت پندرہ روپیہ ہوں تو مبیع ثمن کے ساتھ مضمون ہوگی۔ یعنی وکیل کا موکل پر دس روپیہ کی مقدار ثمن واجب ہے اور موکل کے لئے وکیل پر مبیع کا تاوان مقدار ثمن یعنی دس روپیہ واجب ہیں۔ لہذا نہ وکیل، موکل سے کچھ رجوع کرے گا اور نہ موکل، وکیل سے کچھ رجوع کرے گا۔ بہر حال وکیل کے قبضہ سے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مبیع ضمان رہن کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ضمان بیع کی طرح مضمون ہوگی یعنی جس طرح مبیع اگر بائع کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو مشتری کے ذمہ سے اس کا ثمن ساقط ہو جاتا ہے مبیع کی قیمت خواہ ثمن سے کم ہو خواہ زیادہ ہو۔ اسی طرح جب وکیل کے قبضہ سے مبیع ہلاک ہوگئی تو موکل کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ مبیع کی قیمت ثمن سے کم ہو خواہ زیادہ اور یہی قول امام ابوحنیفہ کا ہے۔

اور امام زفر کے نزدیک وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع ضمان غصب کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ یعنی مبیع اگر ذوات الامثال میں سے تھی تو وکیل پر اس کا مثل واجب ہوگا اور موکل پر ثمن واجب ہوگا اور اگر ذوات القیم میں سے تھی تو وکیل مبیع کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گا۔ چنانچہ اگر مبیع کی قیمت زائد ہو اور اس کا ثمن کم ہو۔ مثلاً قیمت پندرہ روپیہ ہو اور ثمن دس روپیہ ہو تو موکل ثمن سے زائد مقدار یعنی پانچ روپیہ وکیل سے واپس لے گا۔ اور اگر ثمن زائد ہو اور قیمت کم ہو مثلا ثمن پندرہ روپیہ ہو اور قیمت دس روپیہ ہو تو قیمت سے زائد مقدار یعنی پانچ روپیہ وکیل، موکل سے واپس لے گا۔ صدر الشریعہ نے شرح وقایہ میں یہی تفصیل ذکر کی ہے۔ اور امام زفر کے قول کے مطابق یہی تفصیل مناسب بھی ہے۔ لیکن صاحب عنایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر ثمن قیمت سے زائد ہو تو وکیل کو موکل سے کچھ رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر قیمت ثمن سے زائد ہو تو موکل مقدار زائد وکیل سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ بقول علامہ ابن الہمام کے پیشتر شروح سے یہی مفہوم ہے۔ لیکن میرے (علامہ ابن الہمام ) کے نزدیک امام زفر کے قول پر وہی تفصیل ظاہر ہے جو صدر الشریعہ نے ذکر کی ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح قیمت زائد ہونے کی صورت میں موکل کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا ہے۔ بہر حال امام زفر کے نزدیک وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع ضمان غصب کی طرح مضمون ہو گی۔ اس کے قائل ائمہ ثلاثہ ( امام مالک، امام احمد ) ہیں۔ حضرت امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کا اپنے پاس مبیع کو روکنا ناحق طور پر روکنا ہے کیونکہ اوپر کے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے کہ امام زفر کے نزدیک مبیع پر وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے موکل قابض ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور وکیل کو مبیع روکنے کا کوئی حق حاصل نہیں ہے۔ پس جب وکیل کو مبیع روکنے کا کوئی حق حاصل نہیں ہے تو اس کے باوجود وکیل کا اپنے پاس مبیع کو روکنا نا حق طور پر روکنا ہے اور کسی چیز کو ناحق طور پر لینا اور اس کو روک کر بیٹھ جانا غصب ہے۔ لہذا وکیل مبیع روکنے میں غاصب ہوا اور مبیع شیء مغصوبہ ہوئی ۔ پس جب یہ شیء مغصوبہ ہلاک ہوگئی تو وکیل (غاصب) پر ضمان غصب واجب ہو گا ۔ یعنی جس طرح شیء مغصوبہ ہلاک شدہ کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح اس مبیع کا ضمان واجب ہوگا جس کی تفصیل امام زفر کے بیان مذہب کے تحت گذر چکی ہے۔

اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان چونکہ حکما عقد بیع منعقد ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے وکیل بمنزلہ بائع کے ہوگا اور موکل بمنزلہ مشتری کے ہوگا۔ اور بائع کو اپنا ثمن وصول کرنے کے لئے مبیع کو روکنے کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا مبیع کو روکنا بھی موکل سے ثمن وصول کرنے کے لئے ہوگا اور مبیع اگر بائع کے پاس سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو مشتری کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ ثمن خواہ قیمت سے زیادہ ہو یا کم ہو ۔ اسی طرح جب مبیع وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک ہوگئی تو موکل کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ ثمن خواہ قیمت سے زیادہ ہو خواہ کم ہو بہر حال اس دلیل سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ طرفین کے نزدیک وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع ضمان بیع کی طرح مضمون ہو گی۔

علامہ ابن الہمام اور صاحب عنایہ نے طرفین کی مذکورہ دلیل پر ایک اعتراض اور اس کا جواب ذکر کیا ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ اگر واقعی وکیل بمنزلہ بائع کے ہے تو مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں بہر صورت اس پر ضمان واجب ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ خواہ وکیل مبیع کو اپنے پاس روکتا خواہ نہ روکتا۔ کیونکہ مبیع اگر بائع کے پاس سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو وہ بائع پر مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی بائع کے مال سے ہلاک شمار ہوتی ہے۔ اگر چہ بائع نے اس کو نہ روکا ہو۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مشتری کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب وکیل بمنزلہ بائع کے ہے تو اس کے پاس سے ہلاکت مبیع کی صورت میں بھی مبیع اس پر مضمون ہونی چاہئے تھی۔ یعنی مبیع وکیل کے مال سے ہلاک شمار ہونی چاہئے تھی۔ خواہ وکیل اسے روکتا یا نہ روکتا۔ حالانکہ سابق میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اگر وکیل نے مبیع نہ رو کی ہو اور وہ اس کے پاس سے ہلاک ہو گئی ہو تو یہ موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی۔ یعنی موکل کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط نہ ہو گا۔

جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وکیل نے جب اپنے پاس مبیع روک لی تو یہ بات متعین ہوگئی کہ وکیل نے مبیع پر اپنے لئے قبضہ کیا تھا اور جب وکیل نے مبیع پر اپنے لئے قبضہ کیا تھا تو اس کا بائع ہونا یقینی ہو گیا اور جب وکیل کا بائع ہونا یقینی ہو گیا تو مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل پر یقینا ضمان لازم ہو گا۔ یعنی موکل کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط ہو جائے گا اور جب وکیل نے مبیع اپنے پاس نہیں رو کی تو وکیل کا قبضہ کرنا موکل کے لئے ہوگا اور وکیل مبیع کے مشابہ ہو گا اور اس کے پاس سے مبیع کا ہلاک ہونا امانت کا ہلاک ہونا ہو گا۔ اور امانت کے ہلاک ہونے سے امین پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اس مبیع کا ضمان وکیل پر واجب نہ ہوگا بلکہ موکل پر واجب ہوگا۔ یعنی موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی اور موکل کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط نہ ہو گا۔

حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع موکل سے ثمن وصول کرنے کے لئے روکنے کی وجہ سے مضمون ہوئی ہے کیونکہ روکنے سے پہلے مبیع مضمون نہ تھی۔ جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اگر روکنے سے پہلے مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو وہ موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوتی ہے اور وکیل پر اس کا ضمان نہیں آتا۔ بہر حال ثمن وصول کرنے کے خاطر وکیل کے مبیع کو اپنے پاس روکنے کی وجہ سے مبیع مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ اور بعینہ یہی رہن کے معنی ہیں ۔ یعنی جس طرح قرضہ وصول کرنے کے لئے مرتہن شیء مرہونہ اپنے پاس روکتا ہے اسی طرح ثمن وصول کرنے کے لئے وکیل مبیع اپنے پاس روکتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہلاک شدہ مبیع شیء مرہونہ کے مانند ہے اور جب وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع شیء مرہونہ کے مانند ہے تو یہ مبیع ضمان رہن کی طرح مضمون ہوگی اور ضمان رہن کی پوری تفصیل امام ابو یوسف کے مذہب کے تحت گذر چکی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام ابو یوسف کی طرف سے طرفین کے مذہب کو رد کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع عقد
Book of Agency

It will be. For example, an agent for purchase transacted with the seller for fifteen rupees, and the price of the destroyed purchased item is ten rupees, then the purchased item is guaranteed with the price. That is, the principal owes the agent the price, i.e., fifteen rupees, and the agent owes the principal the compensation of the purchased item, ten rupees, so after deducting the ten rupees compensation from the price, the agent will take back five rupees from the principal. And if the price is ten rupees and the value of the purchased item is fifteen rupees, then the purchased item is guaranteed with the price. That is, the agent is owed ten rupees as price by the principal, and the principal is owed compensation for the purchased item amounting to the price, i.e., ten rupees, from the agent. Therefore, neither will the agent recourse against the principal, nor will the principal recourse against the agent. In any case, in the case of the destruction of the purchased item in the possession of the agent, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the purchased item is guaranteed like the guarantee of a pledge. And according to Imam Muhammad, it is guaranteed like the guarantee of a sale, meaning just as if the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the seller, its price lapses from the liability of the buyer, whether the value of the purchased item is less than the price or greater. Similarly, when the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the agent, the price lapses from the liability of the principal, whether the value of the purchased item is less than the price or greater, and this is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa.

And according to Imam Zufar, the purchased item destroyed in the possession of the agent is guaranteed like the guarantee of usurpation. That is, if the purchased item is among things of similar kind, the agent owes its equivalent, and the principal owes the price; and if it is among things of value, then the agent is guarantor for the value of the purchased item. Accordingly, if the value of the purchased item is greater and its price less, for example the value is fifteen rupees and the price ten rupees, then the principal will take back the excess amount over the price, i.e., five rupees, from the agent. And if the price is greater and the value less, for example the price is fifteen rupees and the value ten rupees, then the agent will take back from the principal the excess amount over the value, i.e., five rupees. Sadr al-Shari'ah mentioned this detail in Sharh al-Wiqayah. And according to Imam Zufar's saying, this detail is appropriate. But the author of al-'Inayah mentioned that if the price is greater than the value, the agent has no option to recourse against the principal; and if the value is greater than the price, the principal can take back the excess from the agent. According to the saying of 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam, this is the understanding from most commentaries. But in my (Ibn al-Humam's) view, on the saying of Imam Zufar, the detail that is apparent is the one Sadr al-Shari'ah mentioned, because just as when the value is greater, the principal is given the option to recourse... In any case, according to Imam Zufar, the purchased item destroyed in the possession of the agent is guaranteed like the guarantee of usurpation. This is the view of the three Imams (Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad). The proof of Imam Zufar is that the agent's detention of the purchased item in his possession is wrongful detention, because it has passed in the earlier issue that according to Imam Zufar, by the agent's taking possession of the purchased item, the principal becomes possessor, and the agent has no right to detain the purchased item. So when the agent has no right to detain the purchased item, yet he detains it in his possession, it is wrongful detention, and taking something wrongfully and detaining it is usurpation. Therefore, the agent in detaining the purchased item becomes a usurper, and the purchased item becomes a usurped object. So when this usurped object is destroyed, the agent (the usurper) owes the guarantee of usurpation, i.e., just as the guarantee of a destroyed usurped object is obligatory, similarly the guarantee of this purchased item will be obligatory, the detail of which has passed under the explanation of Imam Zufar's madhhab.

And the proof of the two parties is that because a sale contract is legally (hukman) concluded between the agent and the principal, therefore the agent is like the seller and the principal is like the buyer. And the seller has the right to detain the purchased item in order to collect his price. Therefore, the agent's detention of the purchased item is also to collect the price from the principal, and if the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the seller, the price lapses from the liability of the buyer, whether the price is more than the value or less. Similarly, when the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the agent, the price will lapse from the liability of the principal, whether the price is more than the value or less. In any case, by this proof it is established that according to the two parties, the purchased item destroyed in the possession of the agent is guaranteed like the guarantee of a sale.

'Allamah Ibn al-Humam and the author of al-'Inayah mentioned an objection and its answer regarding the above-mentioned proof of the two parties. The objection is: If indeed the agent is like the seller, then in the case of destruction of the purchased item, guarantee should be incumbent on him in any case, whether the agent detains the purchased item in his possession or not. Because if the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the seller, it is guaranteed on the seller, i.e., it is considered destroyed from the seller's wealth, even if the seller did not detain it. This is why the price lapses from the liability of the buyer. So when the agent is like the seller, then in the case of destruction of the purchased item in his possession, the purchased item should be guaranteed on him, i.e., it should be considered destroyed from the agent's wealth, whether he detains it or not. Although it was previously said that if the agent did not detain the purchased item and it is destroyed in his possession, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth, i.e., the price will not lapse from the principal's liability.

Answer... The answer is that when the agent detained the purchased item in his possession, it became determined that the agent took possession for himself. And when the agent took possession for himself, his being a seller became certain. And when his being a seller became certain, then in the case of destruction of the purchased item, guarantee is definitely incumbent on the agent, i.e., the price will lapse from the liability of the principal. And when the agent did not detain the purchased item in his possession, then the agent's possession is for the principal, and the agent becomes like a trustee, and the destruction of the purchased item in his possession is destruction of a trust, and a trustee is not liable for the destruction of a trust. Therefore, the guarantee of this purchased item will not be incumbent on the agent, but on the principal, i.e., it will be destroyed from the principal's wealth, and the price will not lapse from the principal's liability.

The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the purchased item destroyed in the possession of the agent became guaranteed because of detention for collecting the price from the principal, because before detention, the purchased item was not guaranteed, as has passed earlier that if before detention the purchased item is destroyed in the agent's possession, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth and the agent is not liable for its guarantee. In any case, due to the agent's detention of the purchased item in his possession for the sake of collecting the price, the purchased item becomes guaranteed. And this is exactly the meaning of a pledge, i.e., just as the pledgee detains the pledged object in his possession to collect the debt, similarly the agent detains the purchased item in his possession to collect the price. The conclusion is that the destroyed purchased item is like a pledged object, and when the purchased item destroyed in the agent's possession is like a pledged object, this purchased item will be guaranteed like the guarantee of a pledge, and the complete detail of the guarantee of a pledge has passed under the madhhab of Imam Abu Yusuf. The author of al-Hidayah, refuting the madhhab of the two parties from the side of Imam Abu Yusuf, said that the purchased item destroyed in the possession of the agent is a contract...
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with an important point in the law of agency for purchase: when an agent (wakil) purchases an item for his principal (muwakkil) and then detains the purchased item (mabi') in his own possession to collect the price (thaman) from the principal, and the item is accidentally destroyed in the agent's possession, what are the legal consequences regarding who bears the loss? The passage presents the views of the major Hanafi imams—Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, and Imam Zufar—and their respective analogical reasoning (qiyas). It also includes a refutation by Ibn al-Humam and the author of al-'Inayah against the two parties (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) and a defense of Imam Zufar's position. The passage is a classic example of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the basis of different analogies.

The issue arises because the agent's possession of the purchased item is originally an amanah (trust). However, when he detains it to secure payment, the nature of his possession changes. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the two parties, 'tarafayn') analogize the situation to a sale: the agent is like the seller (ba'i'), the principal like the buyer (mushtari). In a sale, if the item is destroyed in the seller's possession, the buyer's obligation to pay the price is canceled, regardless of whether the price was more or less than the value—the seller bears the loss. Similarly, here, the principal's obligation to pay the price is canceled, and the agent bears the loss. Imam Abu Yusuf analogizes to a pledge (rahn): the agent detains the item like a pledgee detains a pledged object to secure a debt. In a pledge, if the pledged object is destroyed, the debtor's debt is not discharged; rather, the pledgee is entitled to collect the debt from the debtor. Here, the agent detains for the price, so if the item is destroyed, the principal still owes the price, but the agent must compensate the principal for the item's value, resulting in a set-off. Imam Zufar analogizes to usurpation (ghasb): since the agent has no right to detain the item (according to his view, possession vests in the principal immediately), detention is wrongful, making the agent a usurper and the item a usurped object. In usurpation, the usurper is strictly liable for the item; if destroyed, he must pay its value or equivalent. The principal still owes the price, making two claims that are set off.

The passage then presents an objection against the analogy of the two parties: if the agent is truly like a seller, the guarantee should apply even without detention, which contradicts the earlier rule that if the agent does not detain, the loss is on the principal. The answer distinguishes based on the agent's intent: detention indicates he took possession for himself, making him a seller; without detention, he is a trustee.

Finally, the author of al-Hidayah supports Imam Abu Yusuf's view that the item is like a pledge. The passage does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but from the detailed defense, Imam Abu Yusuf's view appears prominent. In practice, later Hanafi fatwa may follow Imam Abu Yusuf or the view of the two parties depending on circumstances. The details of each imam's position regarding set-off (muqassah) are provided with numeric examples.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability/guarantee for a loss; the obligation to compensate for destruction or damage of property.
مضمون (madmun): Guaranteed; property that is subject to liability, meaning its loss must be compensated by someone.
قبض (qabd): Possession; physical control over property. In this context, it distinguishes between possession for oneself (detention) and possession for another (trust).
حكماً (hukman): Legally; in the eyes of the law, as opposed to physically. Used to describe the constructive sale between agent and principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a purchasing agent detains the purchased item to collect the price and it is destroyed, how is the guarantee (daman) treated?
A) Like a sale: the principal's price obligation is canceled entirely.
B) Like a pledge: the principal still owes the price, and the agent owes the value, leading to a set-off.
C) Like usurpation: the agent owes the full value/like and the principal still owes the price, with set-off.
D) Like a trust: the agent bears no liability, and the principal bears the entire loss.

Key Takeaway
The same factual situation—agent detains mabi' for price, then mabi' is destroyed—leads to three different liability rules based on three different qiyas: sale, pledge, and usurpation.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Agent's Liability for Destroyed Purchased Item After Detention
Dispute on whether agent's detention creates liability similar to seller's lien or pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) on agent liability after detention, contrast it with Abu Yusuf's view, and apply the tarjih to a real scenario.

Core Idea
Detention transforms the agent from trustee to seller, making him liable for the destroyed item.

When an agent detains a purchased item to secure payment, does he become like a seller or like a pledgee? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the intra-Hanafi debate between the two parties (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf. The answer determines who bears the loss if the item is destroyed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The issue is whether the agent (wakil) is liable (daman) for the mabi' when it is destroyed in his possession after he detains it to receive the price from the principal.
The detention (habs) is the key trigger.
2
State the position of the two parties
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the agent is like a seller, so the price is dropped from the principal. They argue that the contract between agent and principal is effectively a sale.
They analogize to the seller's right of detention.
3
Examine the objection and response
Ibn al-Humam objects: if agent is like a seller, liability should arise even without detention. The answer is that detention proves possession was for himself; without detention, possession is a trust.
This clarifies that detention is the 'illa.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's alternative analogy
Abu Yusuf says the agent is like a mortgagee (pledgee), and the mabi' is like a rahn. Destruction leads to guarantee on the agent himself, not dropping of price.
He emphasizes the purpose of detention (securing payment), not the legal nature of the relationship.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Sahib al-Hidayah refutes Abu Yusuf's objections and supports the two parties. The contract between agent and principal is annulled upon destruction, establishing similarity with a sale.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two parties.

اگر وکیل بالشراء کے پاس سے مبیع ہلاک ہو جائے تو اصل عقد یعنی وہ عقد جو بائع اور وکیل بالشراء کے درمیان منعقد ہوا تھا۔ فسخ نہیں ہوتا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد بیع کی صورت میں اگر بائع مبیع کو اپنے پاس نہ روکے۔ بلکہ روکنے سے پہلے ہی مبیع بائع کے پاس سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو وہ نفس عقد کی وجہ سے مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی بائع ہی کے مال سے ہلاک ہوتی ہے اور اگر وکیل بالشراء کے روکنے سے پہلے مبیع اس کے پاس سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو وہ مضمون نہیں ہوتی۔ یعنی وکیل پر اس کا کوئی ضمان نہیں آتا۔ بہرحال جب وکیل بالشراء کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع عقد بیع کی مبیع کے مانند نہیں ہے تو وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع، ضمان بیع کی طرح کس طرح مضمون ہو سکتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے طرفین کی طرف سے امام ابو یوسف کی پیش کردہ وجہ فرق کے سلسلہ میں پہلی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے ارشاد فرمایا ہے کہ وکیل کے پاس سے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں اگر چہ وکیل اور اس کے بائع کے درمیان عقد فسخ نہیں ہوتا لیکن وکیل اور اس کے موکل کے درمیان فسخ ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسے اگر موکل مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد مبیع کے کسی عیب پر مطلع ہوا اور عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع وکیل کو واپس کر دی اور وکیل اس عیب پر راضی ہو گیا تو یہ بیع وکیل پر لازم ہو جائے گی اور وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان عقد بیع فسخ ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ وکیل اور اس کے بائع کے درمیان فسخ نہیں ہوا۔ بہرحال جب عقد بیع کی صورت میں بھی بائع کے پاس سے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں عقد فسخ ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور وکیل بالشراء کے پاس سے ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں بھی وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان عقد فسخ ہو جاتا ہے تو دونوں میں مماثلت پائی گئی اور جب مماثلت پائی گئی تو وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ مبیع، ضمان بیع کی طرح مضمون ہوگی جیسا کہ طرفین کا مذہب ہے۔
The argument of the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that since a contract of sale is effectively concluded between the agent and the principal, the agent is in the position of the seller and the principal is in the position of the buyer. And the seller has the right to detain the purchased item to receive his price. Therefore, the agent's detention of the purchased item is also to receive the price from the principal. And if the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the seller, the price is dropped from the buyer's liability, whether the price is more or less than the value. Similarly, when the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the agent, the price will be dropped from the principal's liability, whether the price is more or less than the value. In any case, by this proof it is established that according to the two parties, the purchased item destroyed in the agent's possession is guaranteed like the guarantee of sale. Allamah Ibn al-Humam and Sahib al-Inayah mentioned an objection to this argument of the two parties and its answer. The objection is that if truly the agent is in the position of the seller, then in the case of destruction of the purchased item, guarantee should be obligatory on him in any case, whether the agent detains it or not. Because if the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the seller, it is guaranteed on the seller, i.e., it is considered destroyed from the seller's property, even if the seller did not detain it. This is why the price drops from the buyer's liability. So when the agent is in the position of the seller, then in case of destruction of the purchased item in his possession, the purchased item should also be guaranteed on him, i.e., it should be considered destroyed from the agent's property, whether he detains it or not. Whereas previously it was said that if the agent did not detain the purchased item and it is destroyed in his possession, then it will be destroyed from the principal's property, i.e., the price will not drop from the principal's liability. The answer... The answer to this is that when the agent detained the purchased item in his possession, it became clear that the agent took possession of it for himself. And when the agent took possession of it for himself, his being a seller became certain. And when the agent's being a seller became certain, then in case of destruction of the purchased item, guarantee would definitely be obligatory on the agent, i.e., the price will drop from the principal's liability. And when the agent did not detain the purchased item in his possession, his possession is for the principal, and the agent will be similar to the seller's agent, and the destruction of the purchased item in his possession will be like the destruction of a trust. And with the destruction of a trust, guarantee is not obligatory on the trustee. Therefore, guarantee of this purchased item will not be obligatory on the agent, but rather on the principal, i.e., it will be destroyed from the principal's property, and the price will not drop from the principal's liability. The argument of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the purchased item destroyed in the agent's possession is guaranteed because he detained it to receive the price from the principal, because before detention the purchased item was not guaranteed. As previously passed, if the purchased item is destroyed in the agent's possession before detention, it is destroyed from the principal's property and no guarantee falls on the agent. In any case, due to the agent's detention of the purchased item in his possession for the sake of receiving the price, the purchased item becomes guaranteed. And this is exactly the meaning of pledge (rahn). That is, just as the mortgagee detains the mortgaged property to receive the debt, similarly the agent detains the purchased item to receive the price. The result is that the destroyed purchased item is like a mortgaged property. And when the destroyed purchased item in the agent's possession is like a mortgaged property, then it will be guaranteed like the guarantee of pledge, and the full details of the guarantee of pledge have passed under the school of Imam Abu Yusuf. Sahib al-Hidayah, refuting the school of the two parties from the side of Imam Abu Yusuf, said that the purchased item destroyed in the agent's possession is not like the purchased item of a sale contract. Because in the case of a sale contract, if the purchased item is destroyed in the seller's possession, the sale contract becomes annulled, but if the purchased item is destroyed in the possession of the agent-buyer, the original contract (i.e., the contract that took place between the seller and the agent-buyer) is not annulled. The second proof is that in the case of a sale contract, if the seller does not detain the purchased item in his possession, rather it is destroyed in the seller's possession before detention, then it is guaranteed by the contract itself, i.e., it is destroyed from the seller's own property. But if the purchased item is destroyed in the agent-buyer's possession before his detention, it is not guaranteed, i.e., no guarantee falls on the agent. In any case, when the purchased item destroyed in the agent-buyer's possession is not like the purchased item of a sale contract, then how can the purchased item destroyed in the agent's possession be guaranteed like the guarantee of sale? Sahib al-Hidayah, answering the first proof of the difference presented by Imam Abu Yusuf from the side of the two parties, said that when the purchased item is destroyed in the agent's possession, although the contract between the agent and his seller is not annulled, the contract between the agent and his principal is annulled. For example, if the principal, after taking possession of the purchased item, becomes aware of a defect in it and returns the purchased item to the agent due to the defect, and the agent is satisfied with this defect, then this sale becomes binding on the agent, and the sale contract between the agent and the principal is annulled, even if the contract between the agent and his seller is not annulled. In any case, when in the case of a sale contract, upon destruction of the purchased item in the seller's possession, the contract is annulled, and in the case of destruction in the possession of the agent-buyer, the contract between the agent and the principal is also annulled, then similarity exists between them. And when similarity exists, the purchased item destroyed in the agent's possession will be guaranteed like the guarantee of a sale, as is the school of the two parties.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability (daman) of an agent (wakil) when the purchased item (mabi') is destroyed after the agent detains it. The two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the agent is like a seller vis-à-vis his principal, so if the mabi' is destroyed in his possession after detention, the price (thaman) is dropped from the principal. They analogize to a sale where the seller can detain the item until payment, and if it is destroyed, the buyer is freed from paying. The objection raised by Ibn al-Humam and al-Inayah is that if the agent is like a seller, then destruction should always be on the agent even without detention, just as in a sale. The answer is that detention determines that the agent's possession is for himself; without detention, his possession is for the principal as a trust. Imam Abu Yusuf offers an alternative analogy: the agent's detention is like a pledge (rahn); the agent detains the item to secure payment, just as a mortgagee detains the mortgaged property. Sahib al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) then refutes Abu Yusuf's analogy, arguing that the agent's case differs from a sale because in a sale the contract is annulled upon destruction, whereas the agent's contract with the seller remains intact. However, the two parties respond by noting that the contract between agent and principal is annulled upon destruction, establishing similarity. The Hidayah author's final position appears to support the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that the mabi' is guaranteed like a sale. The passage is a detailed exercise in qiyas and istihsan within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by the principal to perform a legal act, here specifically to purchase an item (wakil bil-shira').
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee for loss; in this context, financial responsibility for the destroyed mabi'.
حبس (habs): Detention of the purchased item by the agent to secure payment of the price from the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what determines whether the agent is liable for the purchased item destroyed in his possession?
A) Whether the agent received the item from the seller
B) Whether the agent detained the item to receive the price
C) Whether the principal authorized the detention
D) Whether the price was paid

Key Takeaway
The agent's detention of the purchased item to secure payment transforms his status from a trustee to a seller, making him liable for destruction and dropping the price from the principal.

Agent Buying More Meat Than Instructed: Binding Quantity
Ruling on how much meat binds the principal when agent buys a larger quantity for the same price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent buys more than instructed, distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn's, and apply the qiyas distinction between quantity and price excess.

Core Idea
Exceeding the specified quantity does not bind the principal, unlike excess price in a sale.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we encounter a classic dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The issue: when an agent buys more meat than instructed but at the same total price, does the principal benefit from the whole, or only the instructed portion? The ruling hinges on the crucial distinction between excess in quantity versus excess in price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
State the exact instructions: the agent is told to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham, but buys 20 ratls for the same price. Note the two positions: Abu Hanifa says only 10 ratls bind the principal at half a dirham; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say all 20 bind at 1 dirham.
Also note that in some copies Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's analogy to slave sale
Abu Yusuf analogizes to an agent instructed to sell a slave for 1000, who sells for 2000. In that case, the entire 2000 belongs to the principal. He argues that the extra meat is similarly a benefit that should accrue to the principal.
The slave sale analogy is the key qiyas used by the Sahibayn.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's distinction
Abu Hanifa distinguishes because in the slave sale, the extra price is in exchange for the principal's property, so it belongs to the principal. Here, the extra meat is not the principal's property; the agent exceeded the specified quantity without authorization. Thus the excess is the agent's own purchase.
This distinction is based on the nature of the excess: price vs. quantity.
4
Apply the ruling to the principal's obligation
The principal is only bound by the instructed quantity (10 ratls) at the proportionate price (half a dirham, since 10 ratls cost half the dirham). The remaining 10 ratls are the agent's responsibility, and the agent must bear the cost or sell them at his own risk.
This protects the principal from unauthorized purchases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا وكله بشراء عشرة ارطال لحم بدرهم فاشترى عشرين رطلا بدرهم من لحم يباع منه عشرة ارطال بدرهم لزم المؤكل منه عشرة بنصف درهم عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يلزمه العشرون بدرهم وذكر في بعض النسخ قول محمد مع قول ابى حنيفة ومحمد لم يذكر الخلاف في الأصل لابي يوسف انه امره بصرف الدرهم في اللحم وظن ان سعره عشرة ارطال فاذا اشترى به عشرين فقد زاده خيرا وصار كما اذا وكله عبده بالف فباعه بالفين ولابي حنيفة انه امره بشراء عشرة ولم يأمره بشراء الزيادة فنفذ شراؤها عليه و ببيع شراء العشرة على المؤكل بخلاف ما اذا استشهد به لان الزيادة هناك بدل ملك المؤكل فتكون له بخلاف ما اذا اشترى ما يساوى عشرين رطلا بدرهم حيث يصير مشتريا لنفسه بالاجماع لأن الأمر اول السـن وهذا مهزول فـ صود الأمر۔
He said: If he appoints him to buy ten ratls of meat for a dirham, and he buys twenty ratls for a dirham from meat of which ten ratls are sold for a dirham, then according to Abu Hanifa, ten ratls are binding on the principal at half a dirham. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: all twenty are binding on him at a dirham. And it is mentioned in some copies the statement of Muhammad with the statement of Abu Hanifa. And Muhammad did not mention the disagreement in al-Asl. For Abu Yusuf, he ordered him to spend the dirham on meat, and he thought its price was ten ratls. So when he bought twenty with it, he did him a favor. And it becomes like when he appoints him to sell his slave for a thousand and he sells him for two thousand. And for Abu Hanifa, he ordered him to buy ten and did not order him to buy the excess. So his purchase of the excess is not executed on him, while the purchase of ten is binding on the principal. Opposite to the case he cited as evidence, because the excess there is in exchange for the principal's property, so it belongs to him. Unlike when he buys what is worth twenty ratls for a dirham, where he becomes a buyer for himself by consensus because the command is regarding the [؟], and this is thin, so the matter is spoiled.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof on a specific case in wakalah: an agent is instructed to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham, but he buys 20 ratls for the same price from a market where the usual rate is 10 ratls per dirham. The text first states the ruling: according to Abu Hanifa, only 10 ratls are binding on the principal at half a dirham (since the agent effectively used half the dirham for the instructed quantity). According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all 20 ratls are binding at 1 dirham. However, it notes that in some copies, Muhammad's view aligns with Abu Hanifa, and that Muhammad did not mention the disagreement in his book al-Asl. Then the reasoning: Abu Yusuf argues that the principal ordered the agent to spend the dirham on meat; the agent assumed the market price was 10 ratls per dirham, so by obtaining 20, he benefited the principal, analogous to the case where an agent instructed to sell a slave for 1000 sells him for 2000 (the extra is for the principal). Abu Hanifa argues that the principal specifically instructed the purchase of 10 ratls; the agent had no authority to buy extra, so the excess is the agent's own purchase. The analogy to the slave sale is different because there the extra price is for the principal's property; here the extra meat is not the principal's property unless authorized. The text also mentions a condition: if the agent buys meat worth 20 ratls for 1 dirham (i.e., at the same rate), he becomes a buyer for himself by consensus because the command is regarding the [؟] and this is weak, so the matter is spoiled. This indicates the ruling depends on the market conditions: if the agent buys at the going rate but in larger quantity, the principal is only bound by the instructed quantity at the proportionate price, while the excess is the agent's responsibility.

Key Terms
رطل (ratl): A unit of weight; here specifically for meat. The standard price is 10 ratls per dirham.
لزم (lazima): To be binding; the purchase becomes binding on the principal, meaning he must accept it and pay the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, how many ratls of meat bind the principal when the agent buys 20 ratls for 1 dirham but was instructed to buy only 10 ratls for 1 dirham?
A) 20 ratls at 1 dirham
B) 10 ratls at 1 dirham
C) 10 ratls at half a dirham
D) None; the entire purchase is the agent's

Key Takeaway
When an agent buys more than the instructed quantity of the same item at the same price, only the instructed quantity binds the principal at the proportionate price; the excess is the agent's responsibility.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Three Scenarios of Agent's Purchase Attribution
Explaining three scenarios of agent's purchase attribution with proofs from custom and sharia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of an agent's purchase attribution and apply the Hanafi ruling for each, including the role of intention and payment in the third scenario.

Core Idea
The agent's purchase is attributed based on how he states the price: to principal, to himself, or absolutely; intention and payment decide ownership.

When an agent (wakil) is appointed to buy an item, the way he states the price determines for whom the purchase is made. Sahib al-Hidayah explains three distinct scenarios based on how the agent attributes the dirhams. Understanding these scenarios is crucial for determining ownership of the purchased item, especially when disputes arise between agent and principal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three attribution scenarios
The agent may attribute the purchase (1) to the principal's dirhams, (2) to his own dirhams, or (3) to absolute dirhams (no attribution). Each leads to a different ruling on ownership.
2
Apply the ruling to the first two scenarios
If attributed to principal's dirhams, the purchase is for the principal. If attributed to own dirhams, it is for the agent. These rulings are supported by custom (urf) and sharia (avoiding ghasb).
Custom dictates that a person buying with his own money buys for himself; attribution indicates agency.
3
Analyze the third scenario based on intention
When dirhams are absolute (e.g., 'I bought this for 100 dirhams'), the agent's intention at the time of purchase decides ownership: if he intended for principal, it is for principal; if for himself, it is for himself. The agent has authority to buy for either.
4
Handle disagreement or lack of intention
If agent and principal disagree on intention, payment (thaman) is decisive: the one whose money paid the price owns the item. If both agree the agent had no intention, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad says purchase is for agent; Imam Abu Yusuf says payment decides.
This step involves the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad as presented in the text.

بہر حال مصنف ہدایہ نے حملاً لحاله على ما يحل له شرعاً سے دلیل شرع بیان کی ہے۔ اور او یفعلہ عادةً سے دلیل عرف کو بیان کیا ہے۔ دلیل شرع تو صرف پہلی صورت پر ہے اور دلیل عرف دونوں صورتوں پر ہے۔ (کفایہ ) تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ وکیل نے عقد شراء کو د راہم مطلقہ کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے۔ مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ غلام ایک سود را ہم کے عوض خریدا اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ اپنے ایک سود را ہم یا موکل کے ایک سو دراہم کے عوض خریدا۔ پس اس صورت میں اگر وکیل نے درا ہم مطلقہ سے مؤکل کیلئے خریدنے کی نیت کی تو یہ عقد شرا ، موکل کیلئے ہوگا اور اگر اپنے خریدنے کی نیت کی تو یہ عقد شراء خود وکیل کیلئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غیر یعین غلام خرید کرنے کی توکیل کی صورت میں وکیل کو دونوں اختیار ہوتے ہیں وہ اپنے لئے خرید کرنے کا بھی مجاز ہے اور مؤکل کیلئے بھی فرید کرنے کا مجاز ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا خرید کرتے وقت جس کی نیت کرے گا غلام اسی کا ہوگا۔ اور اگر دراہم مطلقہ کی صورت میں وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان اختلاف نہ گیا یعنی وکیل نے کہا کہ یہ غلام میں نے اپنے لئے خریدا ہے اور متوکل نے کہا کہ نہیں بلکہ میرے لئے خریدا ہے۔ تو س صورت میں بالاتفاق ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دیا جائے گا یعنی اگر شمن وکیل کے مال سے ادا کیا گیا ہے تو یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی ۔ دور وکیل غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور اگر موکل کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا گیا ہے تو یہ خریداری موکل کیلئے ہوگی اور موکل اس غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔
یونکہ یمن کا ادا کرنا اس بات پر ظاہری دلیل ہے کہ وکیل کے حال کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے۔ جو اس کیلئے شرعاً حلال ہے یا اس کو عادة جاتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر وکیل نے اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا ہے تو یہ اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خریداری خود وکیل کیلئے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عرفا اور عادہ ایسا نہیں کیا جاتا ہے کہ مؤکل اپنے مال سے شمن ادا کرے اور خریداری دوسرے کیلئے ہو اور گر مؤکل کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خریداری بھی مؤکل کیلئے ہے۔ اسلے کہ شرعانیہ بات حرام ہے کہ آدمی خریداری اپنے لئے کرے اور شمن دوسرے کے مال سے ادا کرے جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اس صورت میں وکیل کا غاصب ہونا لازم آئے گا اور اگر وکیل اور مؤکل اس بات پر متفق ہو گئے کہ غلام کی خریداری کرتے وقت وکیل کی کوئی نیت نہیں تھی۔ تو اس صورت میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے: رمیان اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ یہ خریداری، عاقد یعنی وکیل کیلئے ہے کیونکہ اصل پہنی ہے کہ آدمی اپنے لئے کام کرتا ہے ہوائے اس کے کہ وہ اپنا کام کسی دوسرے کیلئے اس کے مال کی طرف نسبت کر کے یا اس کی نیت کر کے قرار دے دے۔ مگر چونکہ یہاں رض کیا گیا ہے کہ وکیل نے اپنی اس خریداری کو دوسرے کیلئے قرار نہیں دیا ہے اسلئے یہ خریداری عاقد یعنی وکیل ہی کیلئے ہوگی ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں بھی ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل بنایا جائے گا۔ یعنی شمن جس کے مال سے ادا ہو گا خریداری اسی کیلئے ہوگی اور وہی غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے جو خریداری کی ہے وہ نیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مطلق ہے اور دونوں صورتوں کا حتمال رکھتی ہے۔ یعنی یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ خریداری موکل کیلئے ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ خریداری خود وکیل کیلئے ہو۔ پس دونوں کا احتمال کھنے کی وجہ سے یہ خریداری موقوف رہے گی۔ یعنی نہ وکیل کیلئے ہوگی اور نہ موکل کیلئے ہوگی۔ بلکہ یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ یمن کس کے مال سے داء کیا گیا ہوگا۔ محتمل خریداری اس کیلئے ہوگی۔ وسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب وکیل اور مؤکل نے اس بات پر اتفاق کر لیا کہ خرید کر تے وقت وکیل کی کوئی نیت نہیں تھی تو اس میں یہ بھی
Sahib al-Hidayah says: This issue has three forms, because the agent will either attribute the purchase contract: (1) to the principal's dirhams, e.g., he says, 'I bought this slave in exchange for the principal's dirhams.' (2) Or he will attribute it to his own dirhams, e.g., he says, 'I bought this slave in exchange for my own dirhams.' (3) Or he will attribute it to absolute dirhams, e.g., he says, 'I bought this slave in exchange for one hundred dirhams' and does not say 'my one hundred dirhams' or 'the principal's one hundred dirhams' – i.e., he did not attribute the dirhams to himself or the principal. ... (continues with explanation of Quduri's phrase, two proofs from custom and sharia, third scenario, and ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Al-Hidayah, explaining the rulings when an agent (wakil) purchases a slave on behalf of his principal (muwakkil). The author identifies three scenarios based on how the agent attributes the purchase price (thaman). The first scenario: the agent attributes the purchase to the principal's dirhams; the purchase is for the principal. The second: the agent attributes to his own dirhams; the purchase is for himself. The third: the agent uses absolute (unattributed) dirhams; then the outcome depends on his intention at the time of purchase – if he intended for the principal, it is for the principal; if for himself, it is for himself.

The author then discusses two proofs cited by Sahib al-Hidayah: (1) 'urf (custom) – people customarily attribute purchases to their own funds, so attribution indicates ownership; and (2) shari'ah – if the agent attributes the purchase to the principal's dirhams but intends it for himself, this involves usurpation (ghasb) which is haram, so such a transaction cannot be valid. The custom proof applies to both scenarios, while the shari'ah proof specifically supports the first scenario (attribution to principal's dirhams leads to principal's ownership).

In the third scenario, if the agent and principal disagree about intention and there is no clear attribution, the payment (thaman) decides the ownership: whichever party's money paid the price, the slave belongs to that party. If they agree that the agent had no intention at the time of purchase, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Imam Muhammad holds that the purchase is for the agent (the contracting party), because a person acts primarily for himself unless he indicates otherwise. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the purchase remains suspended until payment: the one whose money paid the price becomes the owner. This ikhtilaf is based on differing views regarding the role of payment in determining ownership when intention is absent.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): The agent appointed by the principal to perform a task, here to buy a slave.
مؤکل (موکل) (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid in the purchase, here the dirhams.
عرف (urf): Customary practice recognized as a source of law in the absence of explicit text.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation – taking another's property without legal right, which is haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the agent buys a slave with absolute dirhams (e.g., 'I bought this slave for 100 dirhams') and later the agent and principal agree that the agent had no specific intention at the time of purchase, what is the ruling according to Imam Muhammad?
A) The purchase is for the principal.
B) The purchase is for the agent.
C) The purchase is void.
D) The purchase depends on who paid.

Key Takeaway
The agent's purchase attribution depends on how he states the price; when intention is absent, payment decides ownership per Abu Yusuf, or the agent owns it per Muhammad, both valid Hanafi views.
